A quorum-signed `ShardPrepareCertificate` binds the registration/routing proof, stable `(global_txn_id,registration_generation)` prepare key, snapshot, topology/configuration, heads/key epochs, basis/fragment/effect, every witness/constraint/resource/auth/audit commitment, and shard payload availability. Any drift invalidates and rebuilds the affected bases, routing fixed point, aggregate records, fragments, and certificates; digest substitution never recertifies a pre-rebase artifact.

   - **Global certification and decision.** The meta leader admits a commit only with the canonical routing certificate and exact sorted participant set, current distributed-serialization and constraint-reservation certificates, exact expected global prefix/heads/key epochs, and the single aggregate authorization/resource/outcome/terminal-audit bundle. `global_final_effect_digest = H(domain, sorted(participant,basis_effect_digest))`; wrapper fragments and the audit records that bind this digest are excluded from its input. A meta **pre-command-base** availability certificate covers only these already-built objects and explicitly excludes itself and the future command. The completed `GlobalTxnCommand` is then added by the stable prepared-owner successor before proposal. Meta apply assigns the next global logical/commit sequences and HLC, builds the tagged-global marker, atomic head changes, outcome/conflict/constraint state, `GlobalStatePayload`, `GlobalTxnRecord`, and `GlobalStateRoot`—not future shard-produced batches. The quorum then creates a `GlobalDecisionCertificate`, and a following meta control command anchors it in the global certificate registry before any shard may consume it. A failed validation is a typed no-effect global abort that may retain prepares only for deterministic release, adopts no effects, and carries its exact audit outcome. The committed record is the sole commit/abort authority; coordinator loss cannot change it.

   - **Distributed serializability, not “local SSI plus hope.”** Meta-Raft canonically owns `GlobalConflictIndex`. For every registered active or recently completed overlapping serializable transaction—including read-only work—it retains snapshot/start/terminal prefixes, participant set, witness frontier, conservative per-shard read/write summaries, and all `wr`, `ww`, and `rw` edges with proof references until no live transaction can add one. Before commitment, the deterministic certifier replays exact `may_affect` in both directions against every overlapping prepared/committed/closed transaction and rejects FCW/uniqueness conflicts or any cycle. V1 forbids speculative semantic multi-command certification: every commit or read-close certificate is built against the fully applied immediately prior global prefix/conflict/constraint/head state. Group commit may batch fsync/network transport of already sequentially certified entries, but two candidates cannot share a basis or omit cross-candidate edges. Missing/stale support, partition, or resource exhaustion waits or aborts conservatively; monotone coarsening may add false positives only. Read-only results return only after ordered `ReadClose`. An independent SCC/history oracle checks every history, including same-I/O-batch two-writer and rw-cycle cases.

   - **Global constraints and branch authority.** Each cross-partition unique/referential/cardinality domain has a canonical `ConstraintOwner = H(topology_epoch, constraint_id, canonical_domain_key)` shard or an explicitly meta-owned aggregate. The routing certificate lists every owner. Reservations are acquired in canonical `(owner_shard, constraint_id, canonical_key)` order with meta registration order as the deterministic loser/abort priority; participant prepare durably reserves exact keys/ranges and reports before/after contributions, and only an explicit meta decision releases them. Meta certification compares all reservations and aggregate state at the same global prefix and installs them atomically with the decision. Cross-shard path/predicate constraints run over the same registered witness algebra and complete participant closure; an unsupported or incomplete exact evaluator rejects the schema/transaction rather than approximating. Meta state alone owns branch heads/manifests/key-envelope and grant epochs, schema/topology/security epochs, merge/import idempotency, ID-range fences, global capability-verifier roots, and resource/privacy/audit outcomes/continuity. A shard cache is never authority. Every participant uses §12.3's exact `AuthorizedSnapshot`/`AuthorizedMutation` types, and hidden data cannot enter routing, witness, constraint, statistics, or error surfaces.

   - **Apply, visibility, and Ripple.** Participants transition only `None -> Prepared -> GloballyCommitted|GloballyAborted -> Applied -> GcEligible`, keyed first by `(global_txn_id,registration_generation)` and binding the assigned global sequence only when the published decision arrives; duplicate delivery is idempotent. They accept only a meta-anchored `GlobalDecisionCertificate`, apply global decisions in sequence, and cross an irrelevant contiguous range only with `MetaRelevanceRangeProof`; policy/revocation/topology/key/audit fences are never skipped. A query chooses one global prefix and waits/fails until every required shard has applied it, proved irrelevance, and retained that historical prefix; it never silently chooses different cuts. Each committed participant produces its exact fragment batch and signed applied acknowledgement. Meta then builds the complete certified-remote fragment set and orders `GlobalControlCommand(kind=PublishGlobalDeltaBatch)`, which alone advances the global Ripple frontier. Client commit acknowledgement requires that publication, every touched shard's configured apply/durability quorum, terminal audit visibility, and durable outcome; loss before that returns scoped `Unknown`. Per-shard early emission cannot masquerade as a global delta.

   - **Recovery and nonblocking impossibility.** Prepared fragments and their payload certificates stay pinned through a terminal meta decision, participant apply acknowledgements, overlap/retention floors, and consensus GC. A participant never enters `Prepared` without the committed registration and never aborts on timeout, coordinator death, suspicion, or meta unavailability; it recovers its explicit decision from meta-Raft. A signed meta checkpoint plus `GlobalClosedAttemptFloor` may discard only unregistered staging or prove that an attempt generation never became registrable—it can never terminate a valid `Prepared` record. A committed decision is never reversed because a participant is unavailable. Meta and shard joint reconfiguration transfer all commands, decisions, conflict summaries, reservations, prepared ownership, certified-remote obligations, and closed-attempt floors before retirement. This knowingly chooses blocking under the relevant partitions over violating atomicity.

   - **Topology and repartitioning.** Source-range partitioning is the base edge-cut/vertex-owner scheme; optional hub vertex-cut uses separately versioned replicated-vertex metadata and a single canonical edge owner. Movement uses three separately ordered, evidence-complete commands: `TopologyCopyBegin` fixes copy basis `F`, source checkpoint/suffix inventory, joint configurations, and transfer plan while the old owner remains sole write authority; `TopologyCutover` names canonical transfer/catch-up certificates plus the exact active-attempt closure at prefix `S`, stops old-epoch admission, and switches ownership only at `S+1`; `TopologyRetireOld` names every new-owner/meta/backup/key/retention acknowledgement and the final retirement floor. Apply records only evidence already named by its command. No transaction straddles topology epochs, and old bytes/keys cannot retire before the third command. Allocation ranges are meta-fenced before use.

   - **Scope and exit.** These choices are normative now; only their implementation is post-1.0. W12 cannot ship until the dedicated gate in §19 proves meta/shard reconfiguration, every crash/partition point, distributed SCC/constraint histories, cross-shard branch/merge/key/audit behavior, Ripple frontier atomicity, and topology moves. Until that gate passes, a database advertises `sharding=false` and rejects a topology with more than one data shard rather than weakening any 1.0 guarantee.


---

## 15. Determinism, Calibration & Verification Doctrine (Bet B5)

This is not a QA appendix; it is a design pillar with its own budget. It opens with the runtime stratum (§15.0 — the calibration plane that governs the live system), then the verification stack from cheapest to strongest.

### 15.0 Sextant: the calibration discipline within B5

Sextant supplies e-processes, conformal predictors, sequential tests, robust estimators, regime/change detectors, and propensity/OPE tooling as deterministic transformations of logged inputs. It governs performance and operational choices; it never upgrades assumption-bearing evidence into exact correctness.

Every evidence envelope carries `ClaimClass`:

- `SafetyInvariant`: must hold on every execution; failure is a correctness defect.
- `FormalModelClaim`: theorem or model-check result with abstraction, bounds, and refinement status.
- `StatisticalClaim`: population, sampling/selection rule, alpha, power/effective sample size, and assumptions.
- `ConfigurationModelClaim`: model version, fitted inputs, sensitivity, and validity domain.
- `EmpiricalGate`: fixture, machine/profile, sample count, variance budget, and comparison rule.

`invariants.toml` contains only exact safety/liveness obligations. `evidence.toml` contains `FG-CAL-*` and `FG-EVID-*`; `slo.toml` contains `FG-CFG-*`, performance, durability-model, and controller targets. E-processes may be anytime-valid under their named filtration/null assumptions; conformal coverage is marginal under its named exchangeability or online-validity conditions; drift alarms do not retroactively preserve a broken assumption; OPE requires positivity/overlap and sufficient effective sample size. A monitor that drives no named decision is dead code, but binding it to a decision does not make it an invariant.

Every adaptive policy retains a deterministic fallback valid without the statistical model. Answer-affecting execution policies are bound to the `AnswerRequirement`, plan, result contract, and replay closure; canonical-state-affecting promotions are logical-command-sequenced and replay-pinned; only proved answer-preserving physical policies may remain local. Calibration windows, selection policy, strata, propensity support, regime epochs, fallback, and failure behavior are immutable evidence identities. This is how B5 makes adaptation inspectable without confusing “well measured” with “proved safe.”

### 15.1 Simulation-first development (`fgdb-sim`)

The entire database runs under asupersync's lab runtime with virtual time/network/disk, seeded scheduling, chaos, and deterministic pressure models. DPOR is exhaustive only within the declared bounded scenario/state model and the soundness of its independence relation; broader campaigns remain falsification, not proof of bug absence. Every failure still becomes a replayable seed/crashpack, which is the practical value.

Five force multipliers on the same substrate:

- **Targeted falsification (LDFI).** Random chaos asks “what if something fails?”; lineage-driven fault injection derives minimal fault hypotheses from successful-run dependencies. It targets every file/directory action in D1/D2, dual root slots, checkpoint/GC publication, payload availability, and Raft acknowledgement. It is a high-yield falsification tool, while residual random chaos guards lineage blind spots.
- **A model-qualified stopping heuristic.** Novelty estimates and coverage maximization prioritize finite CI time under a named sampling model. They may stop a campaign according to policy; they never certify that no unexplored bug remains. Deterministic bounded-state completion is reported separately from statistical/heuristic stopping.
- **Failing runs shrink themselves.** Hierarchical delta debugging + replay minimization reduce every failing seed (schedule + workload trace) to a minimal reproducer before filing, and divergence diagnostics explain exactly where a replay departed from its recording. Crashpacks arrive pre-shrunk; the bug report writes itself.
- **Lab-vs-live dual runs.** The same scenario, same seed, runs under the lab and against the live build, and the traces are diffed — closing the classic simulation-testing loophole ("we verified the simulator, not the system"). This is the runtime-behavior counterpart of the `fgdb-reference` semantics differential.
- **Production incident replay is graded.** Production retains bounded mediated nondeterminism records under a fail-closed redaction contract. Each bundle carries the explicit `ReplayCompleteness` grade `Replayable | StructuralReplay{reproduced_classes[],omitted_classes[]} | VerifiableIfArtifactsSupplied{missing_classes[]} | AuditOnly{missing_or_redacted_classes[]}`. Crypto entropy is never recorded. Full internal forensic bundles may be exact when policy permits; customer-safe bundles never overclaim byte identity.

### 15.2 Consistency oracles

In-sim checkers include snapshot/branch visibility, an SSI dependency oracle, obligation/quiescence, root/capsule closure, authorization noninterference, and Elle-class histories. The SSI oracle uses a deliberately independent small Tarjan/SCC implementation over trace-derived logical dependencies; production graph algorithms may be a secondary differential, never the sole checker of their own transaction graph. Every invariant has at least one checker outside the optimized component it checks where practical.

Production assertions and complete audits can enforce exact invariants; sampled e-processes are statistical sentinels in `evidence.toml`, not the enforcement column of `invariants.toml`. Replay uses the complete `ReplayManifest` in §8.6. Security verification additionally covers cross-capability differential results/plans/errors/timing classes, revocation during streams, cache/view/index isolation, hidden-state constraints/cascades, donor poisoning, key rotation, restore authorization, parser/resource exhaustion, and audit-chain completeness.

### 15.3 Fault & recovery torture

Crash matrices kill at every D1/D2 file and directory durability point, both root-slot writes, writer-fence takeover, post-rebase capsule finalization, marker batch/root publication, checkpoint authority transfer, compaction safe point, delivery-lease create/ACK/reset, configuration-floor refresh/retirement, each payload-receipt/Raft/apply transition, and every audit phase from external ticket reservation through candidate-root fencing, terminal CAS, mirror command, and visibility publication. Campaigns cover partial marker tails, full-digest collisions in the 128-bit locator bucket, mixed `EncodingId` symbols, erasures within and beyond each source-block budget, multi-process stale writers, uncertain membership/GC, donor poisoning, key loss/two-stage destruction/rotation, and idempotent `Unknown` recovery through a scoped outcome capability. Each scenario declares its failure and placement model.

### 15.4 Differential & conformance testing

- **Semantics oracles**: an executable **reference engine** (`fgdb-reference`) — a deliberately simple, single-threaded, obviously-correct implementation of the full logical semantics (values, visibility, path modes, intents, temporal selectors, branches) over canonical maps, compiled for tests/fuzzing/model-checking only, never shipped, never optimized, so "what should this return" is a program rather than a debate; openCypher TCK; a GQL feature-conformance corpus keyed to ISO feature IDs (published as a matrix); differential vs. Neo4j & Memgraph on a curated corpus (behavior parity where standards align, documented divergence elsewhere); Prism results differential vs. standalone fnx (which is itself NetworkX-parity-locked — a two-hop oracle chain to ground truth). Model-generated histories run against both engines and compare snapshots, results, certificates, and permitted abort outcomes.
- **Storage oracles**: model-based testing of Strata against an in-memory reference graph (arbitrary op interleavings, equality after every op under every open snapshot); metamorphic suites in the house style (e.g., pattern-match results invariant under compaction, seal, branch-fork, encode/decode round-trips).
- **Fuzzing**: parser (GQL/Cypher grammars), FGP frames, every fgdb-formats reader (extending fnx's 8-fuzzer precedent), SymbolRecord decoder.

### 15.5 Formal anchors (scoped, honest — the asupersync posture)

Lean targets the full visibility relation—publication, branch ancestry, create/retire, own writes, and reclamation—not merely three local MVCC facts. SSI work separates: dangerous-structure theorem, lifetime of dependency metadata, soundness of each witness constructor's concretization, refinement preservation of positive/negative/gap/path observations, and optimizer transport of witness obligations. Merge proofs cover the registered algebra in its constraint context. Ripple proofs cover only the explicitly registered operator/annotation subset.

TLA+/TLC models the dual-slot root and schema-complete checkpoint authority transfer, the exact writer-lease/takeover/fence-enable sequence, final-capsule commit, marker/global-branch links, fork-time envelope/write-key double rotation, delivery-lease ACK/resume, audit candidate visibility fencing/external reconciliation, compaction/GC, stable prepared ownership plus payload-availability/Raft, membership reconfiguration floors, branch merge/token/range idempotency, closed-sequence leases, and W12's registered-attempt→participant-prepare→global-certify/decide→barriered-apply protocol, including partitions, meta/shard reconfiguration, conflict-index lifetime, constraint reservations, and topology moves. The generated durable-reference checker separately enforces per-field `PriorObject` construction annotations and rejects cycles in reachable object instances; recursive persistent-tree types remain legal because every concrete parent points only to already identified children. Neither method is mislabeled as the other. Every model run states bounds. Trace export demonstrates that captured executions are allowed by a spec; it is **trace conformance**, not an implementation-refinement proof. Runtime monitors detect selected violations but do not inherit model-check completeness. Proof-lane manifests name abstraction, assumptions, bounds, refinement bridge, and exactly what remains unproved.

Appendix F is the normative design registry. G0 materializes it as checked-in `invariants.toml` with owner, checker path, dependencies, and gate before Genesis implementation begins; the plan does not falsely claim the currently absent file already exists.

### 15.6 Performance regression apparatus

Criterion-style in-house microbench harness + macro suites (§17) with baselines committed, variance-aware gating (the asupersync/fnx baseline artifact discipline), and complexity-witness regression locks: an algorithm or operator whose instrumented operation count exceeds its registered bound on an in-domain fixture fails CI. Correctness, security, durable-format, recovery, authorization, invariant-checker, and required conformance gates are **nonwaivable**. A public, expiring waiver may cover only a named empirical performance threshold, statistical-evidence threshold, or non-safety coverage budget; it records owner, evidence, reduced claim, expiry, and fallback and cannot weaken an invariant or enable a feature whose safety checker failed.

### 15.7 Publish the design

Sortledton/Teseo/Kùzu earned trust by publishing. Target six papers/tech-reports from this work: (1) Strata: temperature-tiered transactional adjacency; (2) One Version Universe: unifying MVCC, temporal, branching, and replication over a fountain-coded commit stream; (3) Refinable predicate witnesses: graph serializability with near-zero false conflicts and no per-edge read tracking; (4) Plan certificates & decision cards: deterministic, auditable query execution; (5) The externally verifiable graph database: transparency checkpoints, inclusion-proof changefeeds, and computed durability certificates over a fountain-coded commit stream; (6) Calibrated adaptivity: anytime-valid statistical governance of a self-tuning DBMS. Ambition includes the receipts.

---

## 16. Observability & Operations

1. **Process tree** (Spork supervision, restart topologies declared):
```
FgdbRootRegion
 ├── ChronicleRegion      (WriteCoordinator · scrubber · checkpointer)
 ├── StrataRegion         (sealers · compactors per partition-group · GC/demotion)
 ├── RippleRegion         (view circuits · subscription fan-out · stats maintainers · index feeders)
 ├── BeaconRegion         (index builders · HNSW mergers · path-index manager)
 ├── PrismRegion          (analytics bulkhead)
 ├── WardenRegion         (policy/revocation authority · lease issuer · DP coordinator · audit anchor)
 ├── AegisRegion          (raft · replication streams · donor service)
 ├── FabricRegion         (listeners · sessions · admission)
 └── ObservatoryRegion    (metrics export · task inspector · spectral health · deadline monitor)
```
2. **Telemetry**: asupersync metrics + OTel export, authorized/redacted trace context, `EXPLAIN`, and `SHOW` surfaces cover transactions, compaction debt, Ripple/index watermarks, buffer residency, resource reservations, obligations, GC membership epoch, key epochs, and commit phases. Little's-law checks and shadow prices are diagnostics under stationarity/model assumptions and live in evidence/SLO registries, not the safety-invariant registry.
3. **Early warning**: wait-graph, futurelock, autocorrelation/variance, and coupled-controller monitors provide model-qualified alerts. `FG-CFG-02` rejects defaults predicted unstable by a versioned fluid model with sensitivity analysis; it does not claim every real workload lies in that model. Hard safety comes from bounded queues, resource reservations, cancellation checkpoints, and deterministic fallback controls.
4. **Ops verbs**: online `COMPACT/SCRUB/REBUILD INDEX/ANALYZE`; `fgdb doctor` verifies root slots, closure, full digests/encodings, marker/branch continuity, constraint state, key wraps, payload availability, GC epoch, and model-qualified configuration reports. Support bundles carry replay-completeness/redaction grades. Cancellation exposes phase and deterministic drain progress; any probabilistic remaining-work/stall estimate names its model and is not a quiescence proof. Quiescence is asserted only when obligations and resource ledgers reach their exact terminal state.
5. **The system graph**: the database's own runtime — sessions, transactions, queries, plans, operators, snapshots + leases, obligations, segments, compaction jobs, subscriptions, replication streams, repairs, decision cards — is exposed as a read-only, access-controlled *temporal property graph*, queryable in GQL like any other graph (`MATCH (q:Query)-[:WAITS_FOR]->(x) WHERE q.elapsed_ms > 250 RETURN q, x`). The wait-for graph is literally a graph: deadlock and contention analysis run Prism's own cycle detection and centrality over it, and incidents become subgraphs you can diff across time. The database dogfoods its data model as its control plane — bounded cardinality, sampled under load, redacted per capability (§12.6).
6. **Admission, backup, and upgrade**: ephemeral hierarchical ledgers reserve/charge/release the transient portion of §13's `ResourceVector`; Chronicle's canonical durable ledger atomically accounts for persistent branches/indexes/views/subscriptions/history/durable bytes through `ResourceChargeEffect`s. Startup/recovery reconciles ephemeral reservations by obligation generation and verifies durable ledger state against committed effects—neither local session counters nor telemetry are quota authority. Maintenance and recovery retain protected emergency capacity. Optimization models may advise allocations, but hard caps and shedding order govern ENOSPC, quorum loss, key unavailability, output backpressure, and tenant isolation.

   Backup is `Authorize -> AcquireRetentionLease -> FreezeRoot -> EnumerateClosure -> Copy -> Verify -> SealSignedManifest -> ReleaseLease`. Canonical `BackupManifest` pins database/security namespace and cluster incarnation, branch heads, logical-command/commit range, root/installed-checkpoint and `CheckpointStateVector`, mandatory and policy-retained object inventory, resume cursors/delivery leases and delivered-output payloads, prepared ownership, incremental-base closure, schema/topology/policy/revocation/key/signing/capability-verifier epochs, recipient wraps, transparency checkpoint, exact current/prospective `ConfigurationState`/floor, external identity/privacy/**audit** continuity plus ticket/event/resolution/CAS-receipt/permanent-gap evidence and resolvers, anti-rollback floors, format matrix, and threshold signature set. Trust policy names accepted signers, threshold, signer-rotation chain, revocations, external anchor, and minimum restorable checkpoint.

   Restore has two noninterchangeable modes. `RecoverSameIdentity` requires an externally recorded fence proving the old cluster cannot continue, verifies the archive/trust/rollback floor, preserves `DatabaseId`, security namespace, `K_oid`, privacy domain, and `AuditDomainId`, advances `cluster_incarnation`, and **CAS-reserves an `AllocationEpoch` strictly above the external `IdentityContinuityRecord` floor before enabling writes**. This burns every possibly issued ID range after the backup even when its database bytes were lost. Before DP is enabled, restore fetches the latest external `PrivacyContinuityRecord`, verifies its predecessor/CAS chain, imports or tombstones every post-backup debit/request, and makes the restored privacy ledger exactly reconcile with that monotonic head. Before any ticket-gated operation is enabled, it likewise fetches the latest `AuditContinuityRecord` and externally retained ticket/event/resolution/CAS-receipt/gap-transition evidence, verifies every direct-successor relation, reconciles every pending and terminal transition, and restores the exact audit chain/status. Unavailable privacy authority disables DP; unavailable audit evidence disables completeness-gated operations. When continuity can resume, only the externally CAS-installed, locally mirrored permanent-gap transition in §12.8 permits operation under its explicitly weakened profile. Neither case is hidden by an incarnation bump.

   Same-identity recovery also resolves or explicitly resets each resume cursor and outstanding delivery lease through ordered commands, invalidates old sessions/capabilities as policy requires, rotates channel/signing/wrap authority, and publishes signed recovery/transparency/identity/privacy/audit-continuity records. Without cluster fencing and allocation continuity, recovery is read-only or must clone. `CloneNewIdentity` assigns a new database/security namespace and `K_oid`, decodes every reachable logical object, rehashes references, re-encrypts/rewraps, rebuilds signatures/accumulators, and verifies the new canonical semantic digest; it is not a metadata rename. It inherits the source **privacy** domain unless an approved disjoint-population policy authorizes a new one. It always creates a new namespace-bound `AuditDomainId` and publishes an `AuditCloneBoundary` signed by source and target authorities, linking the source audit head/evidence scope without pretending old tickets were issued in the target namespace; deployments requiring end-to-end audit lineage retain both chains. Both modes execute `Authorize -> VerifyTrustAndKeys -> Stage -> VerifyClosure -> ReplayAndSemanticDigest -> IdentityModeTransform -> ReconcileExternalContinuity -> AtomicPromote`. Partial staging remains unreachable and is cleaned only by its generation-scoped proof, never a wildcard. RPO/RTO, incremental-base retention, offsite failure domains, key recovery, split-brain fencing, rollback/ID/privacy/audit-continuity detection, and production-format restore drills are deployment gates. Rolling upgrades use a tested format/protocol matrix and rollback point.

---

## 17. Performance Doctrine & Targets

Reference machine: 32-core/64-thread, 256 GB RAM, PCIe-4 NVMe, single node. Every number below is a provisional `EmpiricalGate`, activated only when its benchmark manifest pins CPU/microcode, kernel/filesystem/mount options, NVMe model/firmware and measured fsync distribution, toolchain/build, database configuration, graph/schema, transaction size and concurrency, retention/FEC/encryption/index policy, cold/warm state, result consumption, and statistical comparison rule. External “best” comparisons pin a publication, version, dataset, and configuration; moving or unavailable comparators cannot be CI gates.

| Domain | Gate |
|---|---|
| Cold bulk load (CSV/Parquet-lite → sealed runs) | ≥ 40M edges/s sustained (I/O-bound: ≥ 60% of NVMe seq-write ceiling) |
| Transactional ingest | Provisional ≥ 2M edge inserts/s for the pinned batch/txn mix; latency includes final rebase/constraint work, payload D1, root D2, configured encryption/FEC, and in replicated mode payload quorum + Raft. No marker-only benchmark is reported as commit latency. |
| Tier-migration churn | report promote↔demote reversals per descriptor, minimum-dwell violations (must be zero), conversion-cost regret, and soak-test limit cycles. SPRT type-I/type-II bounds apply only to its declared decision hypotheses; they are not reversal-rate bounds. |
| Point reads (vertex by key, 1-hop existence) | ≥ 8M lookups/s across cores; p99 < 15 µs warm |
| Neighbor scans, sealed runs (decoded-cache path) | ≥ 500M edges/s per core; ≥ 10B edges/s node aggregate (memory-bandwidth-bound: EF+varint decode ≥ 4 B/edge effective) |
| 2-hop factorized count (10⁸-flat-row equivalent) | < 50 ms (factorization gate: must not materialize) |
| Triangle count (WCOJ over compressed runs), e.g. com-Orkut-class | within 2× of best published static-CSR WCOJ systems; ≥ 20× any pointer-chasing GDBMS |
| LDBC SNB Interactive SF-100 | full compliance run; throughput ≥ 3× Neo4j, ≥ 1.5× best published embedded engine on reference class |
| LDBC Graphalytics (BFS/PR/WCC/CDLP/LCC/SSSP) | within 1.5× of dedicated static analytics engines *on transactional storage* (the Sortledton bar, beaten) |
| LDBC FinBench (write-heavy, temporal-flavored) | publishable leadership run |
| Time-travel query overhead | Measure current OLTP cost by retention policy plus historical latency by checkpoint distance and suffix bytes; provisional targets are <8% current-path overhead and <2.5× for the declared recent-history fixture, not universal guarantees. |
| Vector: 10M × 768-d f32, HNSW | Provisional ≥20k QPS at measured recall ≥0.95 on a pinned authorized-snapshot corpus; publish exact-baseline sampling and confidence interval. Separately report logical commit→delta-tail searchable and commit→merged-generation latency. No sample can “certify” each insert. |
| Ripple view maintenance | delta application ≥ 1M input-changes/s per circuit worker; subscription end-to-end p99 < 10 ms |
| Branch create / snapshot open | Snapshot open is O(1) metadata and provisional <100 µs warm. Durable branch creation is O(1) data-copy complexity but includes root publication/fsync or Raft and has a separate latency distribution. |
| Recovery (clean shutdown / crash @ 1 TB) | < 1 s / < 30 s to first query (anchor-mapped, capsule tail replay) |
| Temporal connectivity (`CONNECTED … AS OF`, sealed history) | Provisional <100 µs per probe over every sequence sampled by the pinned sealed-history fixture. The result is exact only for a matching `sealed-exact` projection/root; branch overlays or uncovered tails must be compensated or fall back (§10.7). |
| Cardinality-interval evidence | Report realized marginal coverage, stratum counts, selection/window policy, drift alarms, and any nonexchangeability penalty; failure reverts to conservative costing. This is `FG-CAL-02`, not a correctness gate. |
| Tail evidence | p99.9 is empirical when sufficiently observed; any POT/GPD extrapolation separately reports threshold, exceedance count, dependence/stability diagnostics, fit uncertainty, and sensitivity. A model failure blocks the extrapolated claim rather than “certifying” the tail. |
| Durability model | Modeled MTTDL ≥ declared target with sensitivity bounds for every shipped profile (`FG-CFG-01`); crash/restore tests remain separate empirical evidence. |
| Controller stability | Defaults outside the named model's predicted instability region with sensitivity margin (`FG-CFG-02`) plus no limit cycle in pinned soak fixtures. |
| Adaptive-policy audit | Promotion requires the registered `FG-CAL-01` evidence rule, overlap/effective-sample checks, and deterministic fallback; reports never claim arbitrary-policy OPE. |

Method: every gate has a bench binary, a committed baseline, a variance budget, and a flamegraph artifact on regression; the harness itself is deterministic (seeded workloads, pinned schedules) so regressions replay. Performance work follows the asupersync "How We Made It Fast" discipline: profile → remove one contention/allocation → re-verify determinism and cancel-correctness → commit with evidence — one lever per change, never a bundle. Five standing laws bind every published number: (1) *no benchmark-only semantics* — durability, isolation, and result consumption match the declared production mode; (2) *distributions, not averages* — p50/p95/p99/p99.9 and worst hot-key behavior are always reported, with extreme quantiles carrying their fitted-tail confidence intervals rather than raw sample maxima; (3) *never hide compaction* — foreground latency during compaction, checkpoint, GC, and index build is part of the result; (4) *memory is a first-class metric* — bytes per live edge include versions, indexes, witnesses, and allocator slack, not just payload; (5) *adaptive numbers disclose their policy epoch* — any result produced under a non-fallback policy names it, and the fallback's number is published beside it.

---

## 18. Workspace Layout & the Build-It-Ourselves Inventory

### 18.1 Crates (`fgdb-*` workspace, layered; Cargo-enforced boundaries per frankensqlite)

| Layer | Crates |
|---|---|
| Foundation | `fgdb-types`, `fgdb-bigint` (canonical exact integers), `fgdb-delta-types` (G0/W2 delta schema only), `fgdb-claim`, `fgdb-authz-types`, `fgdb-policy` (restricted verifier IR), `fgdb-resource`, `fgdb-codec`, `fgdb-sketch`, `fgdb-collections`, `fgdb-crypto`, `fgdb-calibrate`, `fgdb-evidence` |
| Unsafe islands | `fgdb-unsafe-simd`, `fgdb-unsafe-arena`, `fgdb-unsafe-vfs` — the only crate roots not using `forbid(unsafe_code)`; every site is ledgered and exposed only through safe APIs |
| Chronicle | `fgdb-ecs` (identity/encoding/bootstrap/object locator), `fgdb-order` (durable Raft log/state core and quorum-one driver), `fgdb-chronicle` (capsule/marker/logical-local roots, allocator, outcomes, checkpoints/retention, recovery/GC/scrub), `fgdb-branch`, `fgdb-keymgr`, `fgdb-audit`, `fgdb-backup` |
| Strata | `fgdb-strata` (label-independent tiers, seal/compact, stable-ID directory), `fgdb-props`, `fgdb-buffer`, `fgdb-scratch` |
| Txn + secure access | `fgdb-txn` (MVCC, Graph-SSI/witness lifecycle, coordinator, final-effect merge ladder), `fgdb-constraints` (branch-scoped canonical enforcement), `fgdb-secure-view` (sole authorized storage/permit facade); depends on Chronicle + Strata + foundation policy verifier |
| Loom | `fgdb-gql` + `fgdb-cypher` (syntax only), `fgdb-bind`, `fgdb-algebra`, `fgdb-planner`, `fgdb-exec`, `fgdb-linalg`, `fgdb-datalog`; all reads flow through `fgdb-secure-view` |
| Ripple | `fgdb-ripple` (Z-sets, circuits, incrementalizer), `fgdb-views`, `fgdb-subs` |
| Beacon | `fgdb-index-core`, `fgdb-btree`, `fgdb-fts`, `fgdb-vector`, `fgdb-pathidx` (2-hop/landmark + the persistent-union-find temporal-connectivity index, §10.7) |
| Prism | `fgdb-prism` (authorized projection bridge, fnx cursor/cache/materialization paths, native kernels) |
| Warden | `fgdb-warden` (issuance/revocation/discharges/policy admin), `fgdb-privacy`, `fgdb-redaction` |
| Surface/operations | `fgdb-protocol` (FGP state machine), `fgdb-bolt`, `fgdb-formats`, `fgdb-udf-vm`, `fgdb-observatory`, `fgdb-system-graph` |
| Aegis | `fgdb-raft` (multi-member protocol over `fgdb-order`), `fgdb-repl` (payload availability, anti-entropy, reconfiguration, fenced GC); future `fgdb-shard` belongs only to W12 |
| Composition | `fgdb` (embedded API), `fgdb-server` (top-level Fabric+Warden+Aegis composition), `fgdb-cli`, `fgdb-python` (allowed fnx-python packaging boundary only) |
| Verification | `fgdb-sim`, `fgdb-reference` (executable semantics oracle), `fgdb-oracles`, `fgdb-bench`, `fgdb-conformance`, `fgdb-fuzz` |

G0 materializes `invariants.toml`, `evidence.toml`, `slo.toml`, the unsafe-boundary ledger, feature/conformance matrices, threat model, format registries, proof-lane manifests, and exit-criteria contracts before Genesis implementation.

### 18.2 Built in-house (because the universe is closed)

Compression codecs (EF, delta-varint, bitpacking, snappy, roaring-like), canonical signed-limb exact integers, sketches, ART/radix structures, succinct rank/select, vectorized hash tables, B-tree, HNSW + quantizers + IVF-PQ cold tier, persistent union-find, masked-semiring SpMV/SpMSpV kernels, inverted index + BM25 + Levenshtein automata, tokenizers, CSV/JSONL/Parquet-lite readers, GQL/Cypher parsers (hand-written recursive descent + Pratt — the frankensqlite parser school), the DBSP-style circuit runtime, Raft, FGP, Bolt subset, crypto profiles/primitives not already supplied by an audited foundation, the MMR accumulator + transparency checkpoints, the Sextant calibration scores/ledgers (over asupersync's e-process core), the deterministic UDF bytecode VM (§13.8), bench harness. **Explicitly not built**: async runtime, scheduler, channels, TLS/QUIC/HTTP/gRPC stacks, RaptorQ, macaroons, metrics/OTel, deterministic lab, supervision, cluster membership (SWIM+Lifeguard), Merkle-range anti-entropy, coded symbol distribution, CRDT obligation ledgers, HLC, choreographic projection, LDFI/delta-debug/dual-run/trace-export tooling, Kafka/JetStream clients — all asupersync; graph algorithms & legacy formats — all fnx. The closed-universe constraint, which sounds like an albatross, is the moat: the entire dependency surface is auditable, deterministic under lab, and owned.


---

## 19. Workstreams & Convergence Gates

No MVP and no substitute architectures. Work is sequenced by dependency and converges through constitutional gate G0 plus four integration gates. Sharding is W12 after 1.0 and cannot weaken the single-node/replicated contracts.

**Gate G0 — Constitutional Contracts:** before Genesis code, land the threat/trust model; six-bet vocabulary; exact twenty-invariant spine; `invariants.toml`, `evidence.toml`, and `slo.toml`; generated durable-schema/reference-kind/**acyclic-construction** registry, including every reserved W12 kind and role-tagged Raft/root/checkpoint variant; full logical/ciphertext/complete-encoding/non-self-referential-placement identity and self-sufficient root bootstrap; dual-slot/local root plus versioned filesystem profile and exact lease→recover→fence-root→enable takeover protocol; layered `LogicalStatePayload`/command/root, the exact three-phase bootstrap, stable prepared ownership, normative pre-order command/applied-result split, logical-command sequence/HLC, projected-basis `CheckpointStateVector` plus mandatory genesis or paired operational checkpoint/floor install, exact `ConfigurationState`/cuttable weak-checkpoint-observing floor, exact-cut Raft snapshots, and quorum-one state machines; externally fenced stable ID allocator plus privacy and audit continuity; branch-scoped constraints, constructive key-envelope DAG/fork double rotation/recipient grant, pre-minted merge-token/imported-range idempotency ledger, and disclosure contracts; policy IR/permit types; two-stage key lifecycle/destruction proof; resource/DP/submission+abort outcome/audit admission plus authorization/terminal gates, transaction/control event, resolution/mirror/gap states; distinct answer-requirement/approximation-profile/result-contract plus replay evidence-slot/registry/archive contracts; conditional delta-template and self-contained retained-batch schemas; publicly digested delivered baseline/delta payloads, keyed envelope ID, durable resume cursor, and tagged baseline/delta lease registry; all four cross-session capabilities and their exact FGP issue/present fields; GLA operator and answer-transfer schema; frozen tagged `LanguageContract`s for every advertised surface, including the GQL 1.0 contract's ISO minimum closure, `GG01` or `GG02` plus one of `GG20`–`GG23` as applicable, all prerequisites, synchronous Unicode/UTS #10/UAX #15/UAX #31 bundle, and optional IDs plus exact openCypher/FQL/Datalog profiles; proof-lane manifests; and checker ownership. G0 also synchronizes README/AGENTS summaries and validates their normative examples against these registries. It runs self-containment, dependency-DAG, justification, and fresh-review checks. No workstream may invent a missing semantic choice locally.

| WS | Name | Contents | Depends on |
|---|---|---|---|
| W1 | Bedrock + security foundations | scalar/bigint/delta/claim/authz/policy/resource/codec/crypto/evidence types; unsafe islands/ledgers; lab VFS/sim; reference semantics; generated format parsers and policy verifier | G0 |
| W2 | Chronicle contracts + durability core | self-sufficient bootstrap and metadata-key AAD; dual-slot root under the versioned filesystem profile and exact writer-takeover fence state machine; three-phase logical payload/command/root plus local/prepared roots; stable prepared ownership; complete encoding versus descriptor-derived placement identity; allocator/privacy/audit continuity; pre-order specs versus applied records; capsule, normative command, logical-command record, marker, and two-sequence state machines; quorum-one Raft ordering and exact-cut snapshots; projected-basis checkpoint plus mandatory genesis/paired-operational install; exact configuration schema and weak-checkpoint-observing floor; canonical final-effect→conditional-coordinate `LogicalDeltaTemplate`→self-contained marker-identified `LogicalDeltaBatch` differential; branch-scoped constraint/resource/submission-abort outcome/key-envelope+fork/pre-minted merge/privacy/DP/replay/delivered-baseline+delta cursor/audit admission+terminal+mirror+gap records; retention, two-stage key destruction, backup, and payload interfaces | W1 |
| W3 | Strata | label-independent tiers, stable-ID directories/ordinal maps, property storage, buffer/scratch, checkpoints, bulk/seal/compaction and physical equivalence | W1, W2 object/snapshot interfaces |
| W4 | Transactions + Secure View | MVCC/SSI/witness lifetime, branch-scoped constraint enforcement, canonical locking, coordinator/rebase/final effects, authorization permit verification, authorized cursor/view/mutation facade | W1 policy verifier, W2, W3 |
| W5 | Loom | syntax → binder → complete GLA → planner/stats → factorized/spillable executor/path semantics; compositional `AnswerContract`; authorization-, witness-, and exactness-preserving rewrites | W2 snapshots, W3 storage, W4 txn/secure view |
| W6 | Ripple | consume W2's canonical delta contract; exact Z-sets, derivative=batch laws, validated recursion, policy-labeled table/graph views, subscriptions/resets | W2 committed effects/delta schema, W5 algebra |
| W7 | Beacon | watermark/tail-correct rebuildable property/adjacency/FTS/vector/path indexes; authority domains; optimized adapters for W4 canonical constraints, never duplicate ownership | W3, W4 constraints/secure view, W5 planner, W6 feeds |
| W8 | Prism + fnx upstream | authorized projection spec, cursor/GAT upstream work, spillable materialization/external algorithms, native kernels | W1 authority, W3, W4 secure view, W5 semantics |
| W9 | Warden | issuance/revocation/discharges, policy administration, constraint declassification/noninterference, irreversible-before-access DP state, two-stage reachability-fenced key lifecycle, externally monotonic ticket-gated audit/redaction and rollback reconciliation, replay-resolver and observability authority | W1 verifier/crypto, W2 roots, W4 secure view, W6–W8 derived domains |
| W10 | Fabric + operations | bounded FGP/subscription state machines; HTTP/gRPC/WebSocket/Bolt adapters; admission/QoS; backup/restore; CDC; CLI/server/Python/system graph | W2–W9 |
| W11 | Aegis replication + HA | extend W2's quorum-one Raft to multi-member consensus; stable prepared-owner payload availability, joint/final/final-retirement-floor reconfiguration, safe GC, anti-entropy/seeding, follower security/data fences, witnessed transparency | W2 commit/payload/Raft interfaces, W9 authority, W10 protocol/status contracts |
| W12 | Post-1.0 sharding | meta-Raft-only semantic time; registered attempts; shard D1/Raft prepares and availability certificates; exact global effect aggregation; meta-owned dependency-graph certification and overlap lifetime; deterministic constraint owners/reservations; atomic global branch/key/outcome/audit state; one-prefix apply barriers and complete global Ripple batches; closed-attempt recovery; joint meta/shard reconfiguration and fenced topology moves | 1.0/G4 and W11; dedicated W12 gate below |

**The Genesis slice.** The first W1–W5 integration begins by proving `Genesis -> CheckpointInstalled -> Operational`, including crashes before/after each checkpoint/floor command, and admits no user operation earlier. It then exercises final abstractions end to end: authenticated authority → pinned GQL `LanguageContract`/Unicode bundle/binder/role-bearing graph references → typed GLA subset → planner → authorized Strata cursor → positive/absence/path witness → SSI/constraint validation → forced base drift and new post-rebase capsule under `IntentSemanticsOid` → D1/D2 logical/local-root publication → crash recovery from both slots and the installed checkpoint → canonical result + executable `ReplayManifest`. It includes stable IDs under label mutation, factorized/flat equivalence, spill, one safe replan class, and a correctly typed decision card. The lab explores declared bounded interleavings and differentials against independent semantics/oracles. No stub transaction, post-filter security, pre-rebase capsule, or parser-interpreted execution qualifies.

**Gate G1 — "The Engine Lives":** three-phase bootstrap and embedded authorized path; bounded resources; declared GQL/Cypher feature subset, synchronous Unicode bundle, and matrix; acyclic durable-object construction; final-capsule/command/pre-minted-merge coherence; stable D1 prepared-root ownership and quorum-one ordered-command crash recovery; generated complete projected checkpoint-vector + mandatory genesis/paired-operational checkpoint-floor install + logical-command/transaction-marker suffix recovery with no historical-floor retention chain; exact Raft snapshot cut binding; serializable witness families formally and independently validated; accepted-filesystem conformance plus lease-owner-death/fence-root-before-enable/torn-root/marker-tail/stale-writer/bootstrap/recovery matrices green; constraint state authoritative; compaction/label changes preserve logical digests; strict canonical replay closure works; every implemented invariant has a live checker. Full language breadth is not claimed until its binder/operator rows exist.

**Gate G2 — "One Version Universe":** verified schema-complete checkpoint-install+logical-command suffix recovery and per-graph retention over mixed transaction/control commands; branch fork double rotation, exact envelope DAG/AAD and `StrongCiphertextRef` realization retention, snapshot/advancing handoff, re-encryption/movement under live grants, sibling/post-fork-parent non-decryption, and pre-minted merge-token/imported-range-idempotent explicit-base merges across history cuts; conditional source templates plus self-contained retained Ripple batches; publicly authenticated baseline results and atomic/coalesced delta provenance/output; durable cursor-generation plus tagged baseline/delta lease, baseline-ACK/delta-ACK/resume/lost-response/expiry recovery with no delta-before-baseline or silent gap; table/graph views with explicit read policies; watermark/tail-correct indexes; historical/capability-safe ANN roots with exact fallback; authorized Prism projections; backup/restore round trip including all external continuities and key-envelope/grant roots; empirical/statistical gates reported with assumptions.

**Gate G3 — "Verified & Networked":** bounded FGP connection/transaction/query/stream/FEC machines and adapters, including exact `SymbolRecord`, baseline/delta digest transport and ACK/resume, cursor generations, and explicit issue/present grammar for all four cross-session capabilities; end-to-end Warden noninterference plus declared constraint declassifications, revocation, externally monotonic irreversible-before-access DP debit and rollback reconciliation, two-stage reachability-fenced key destruction, exact audit ticket admission→authorization gate→typed transaction/control event→terminal gate→candidate→external-CAS→mirror continuity with nonrecursive lifecycle gates, rollback reconciliation and durable permanent-gap transitions, and restore authorization; multi-member Raft prepared-root payload ownership/availability before ordering, exact stable/joint configuration semantics, weak-checkpoint-observing final retirement floor paired with checkpoint replacement, exact-cut snapshots, leader-loss at every phase, two-prefix fenced follower reads, all-typed-root consensus GC, and idempotent unknown/abort outcomes; local rollback, witnessed-detection, and witnessed-non-equivocation claims remain distinct, with quorum-intersection, durable witness state, consistency, freshness, cross-log and joint-rotation matrices green wherever prevention is claimed; raw versus filtered proof scopes correct; formal/model claims and implementation bridges landed before their advertised guarantees.

**Gate G4 — "Leapfrog, Published":** all activated §17 benchmark manifests green/public; 100% of G0's 1.0 `LanguageContract`—ISO minimum closure, `GG01` or `GG02` plus one of `GG20`–`GG23` as applicable, all prerequisites, required scalar profile, validated synchronous Unicode/UTS #10/UAX #15/UAX #31 bundle and UCS_BASIC behavior, and named optional IDs—passes its ISO-ID/TCK corpus, while every out-of-contract feature is rejected/documented; canonical replay/archive/answer requirement/profile/result-contract and security matrices; production-format recovery/restore/continuity drills; crash-fault multi-writer preparation and globally ordered commitment; evidence reports correctly qualified; papers match proven scope; 1.0. W12 sharding is excluded and cannot reuse G4 evidence as its gate.

**Gate W12 — "One Universe, Many Shards" (post-1.0):** every reserved kind has an exact encoder/decoder/reference row; role-tagged local/meta/shard Raft logs and exact-cut snapshots reject cross-role commands; every semantic mutation, including single-shard work, enters meta-Raft and receives the one global logical/transaction/HLC order. Registration precedes every serializable read; read close is a global control; effect-only bases, fixed-point routing, one union-wide authorization/audit decision, fence-free canonical prepares, typed constraint/serialization certificates, pre-command-base availability, decision anchoring, shard apply, and post-decision global-delta publication pass DAG and crash proofs. Every cross-group edge passes two-sided `CertifiedRemoteStrongRef` retention/GC tests; every participant prepare has durable availability and exactly one terminal decision; no timeout aborts or atomicity fractures under crash/partition/leader loss/reconfiguration. The independent global SCC/history oracle finds no committed cycle across local, cross-shard, negative/gap/path, read-only, and batch interleavings; deterministic unique/referential/cardinality/path owners/reservations agree with a single-threaded global reference. Branch/key/ID/security/resource/privacy/audit state is meta-atomic; every cross-shard read uses one retained barriered prefix; Ripple advances only after the complete certified fragment set is meta-published. Three-phase topology copy/cutover/retire tests prove no ambient evidence, straddled epoch, or premature byte/key retirement. Meta and every shard pass payload/certificate loss, checkpoint+suffix, donor loss, backup/restore, and rolling-upgrade matrices; activated FG-INV-01–20 clauses all have live checkers; published benchmarks disclose the global sequencer ceiling. Only then may feature negotiation advertise `sharding=true`.

---

## 20. Risks & Mitigations

| Risk | Reality check | Mitigation |
|---|---|---|
| Scope: this is a multi-hundred-KLOC system | True — and smaller than frankensqlite, on stronger foundations | Agent-swarm methodology with ledger-driven exit criteria (proven twice in-family at this scale); sim-first testing collapses the debugging tail that normally dominates DB schedules; crate boundaries sized for parallel agents |
| Free-Join + factorization + adaptivity interplay is the hardest novel engineering | Correct — this is the crown-jewel risk | Build order inside W5: binary FreeJoin → run-trie WCOJ → factorized columns → adaptivity; each stage gets independent semantic and benchmark evidence; published artifacts are behavioral references, not inherited certificates. |
| Graph-SSI phantom/path witness design could be unsound | Central correctness risk | SERIALIZABLE rejects unverified witness families; formal concretization/may-affect proofs, optimizer-preservation laws, independent small-model histories, and gap/negative/path mutation tests gate each family. SNAPSHOT is an explicit weaker contract, not containment for a false serializable claim. |
| HNSW under MVCC/capabilities/compaction | Known-hard industry-wide | Pin historical authorized topology roots, compensate complete delta tails, retain exact fallback, and label recall evidence by population. Output filtering and exact rerank cannot repair missed candidates. |
| Adaptive tiering thrashes (representation churn eats its own benefit) | The classic failure mode of every adaptive store | SPRT migration cards with indifference-region hysteresis and model-conditional type-I/type-II evidence (§6.6); benefit must exceed conversion cost + uncertainty; pinned deterministic fallback policy under lab; observed migration churn is a separate gated §17 metric |
| Witness refinement becomes a second query (cost eats the abort savings) | Possible on pathological predicates | Refinement is budgeted with conservative-abort fallback; `WitnessTrace` is a byproduct of normal execution (no re-execution); refined-vs-saved accounting on every decision card; the knob defaults conservative |
| Nightly Rust | Both foundations already pin nightly; MSRV churn is real | Pinned toolchain per repo (house pattern), portable-SIMD isolated behind `fgdb-codec`/kernel traits with scalar fallbacks |
| fnx algorithms not yet trait-generic or external-memory where required | Verified: `GraphView` exists with integer rows; compatible larger-than-memory coverage is partial | W8 upstream/cursor work plus spillable materialization and family-specific external algorithms. Unsupported functions remain unregistered—there is no “always-correct fallback” that secretly requires the whole graph in RAM. |
| Final-capsule encoding and quorum distribution limit commit throughput | Correctness requires them before publication | Pipeline/group finalization after coordinator-approved effects, benchmark the complete D1/D2/Raft path, and optimize only after effect-digest and availability invariants remain green. |
| Root/checkpoint/retention protocol loses recovery closure | Catastrophic | Dual root slots, full closure validation, checkpoint authority transfer, stale-writer fencing, two-root GC accounting, and crash matrices at every file/directory barrier. |
| Kùzu's fate as a cautionary tale (great engine, no oxygen) | The sharpest non-technical risk | FrankenGraphDB is an open-source ecosystem asset; B1/B4/B5/B6 target agent memory, auditability, and governance without making ungrounded market guarantees. |
| The calibration plane becomes ornamental math (monitors nobody gates on) | The classic fate of statistical infrastructure | Every Sextant artifact binds to a named decision card, `evidence.toml` row, or `slo.toml` row—or is removed as dead instrumentation. It can gate an adaptive promotion or empirical claim but never masquerades as an invariant checker. |
| Adaptive policies diverge logical results | Fatal | FG-INV-19 separately pins answer-affecting choices in the bound/replay closure and logical-command-sequences canonical-state-affecting policy epochs; answer-preserving physical classification has equivalence tests and replica logical-digest oracles. Physical encodings need not be identical. |
| Statistical guarantees rest on modeling assumptions | Unavoidable | Every claim names assumptions and scope; monitoring can trigger fallback but does not retroactively restore invalid coverage. Safety remains independent of statistical success. |
| In-house cryptography fails despite vectors | High-impact specialized risk | Prefer audited foundation primitives; constant-time/misuse verification, algorithm agility, independent review, and external release audit are mandatory. |
| Planner-only authorization leaks through another path | Unacceptable | `fgdb-secure-view` is the unforgeable access boundary for storage, indexes, Prism, Ripple, UDFs, backup, errors, and observability; cross-capability differential matrices gate releases. |
| Global meta sequencing preserves semantics but may bottleneck post-1.0 sharding | Deliberate correctness/performance tradeoff | The protocol is fixed in §14.6: no shard-local semantic bypass, exact global certification and one-prefix visibility. Batch/pipeline the meta order and publish the ceiling honestly; reopen scalar time only as a new architecture with new Chronicle/branch/Ripple/replay proofs, never as an optimization. |
| Newer runtime surfaces adopted for Aegis (choreographic codegen, coded fan-out) prove less mature than core asupersync | Adoption risk, inherited not created | Each adoption sits behind a protocol trait with the hand-built degenerate mode preserved (static membership, unicast fan-out, hand-written state machines); the lab's dual-run harness compares adopted vs. degenerate paths before any promotion |

---

## Appendix A — On-Disk Object Formats (normative contract)

All durable encodings use a declared format major/minor, little-endian fixed integers, canonical unsigned LEB128 only where the field says varint, length-before-allocation, checked arithmetic, and per-kind maximum sizes. Unknown additive-minor fields are length-delimited and skipped; unknown required flags fail closed. `CanonicalScalarProfile` defines float/decimal/string/time bytes. Readers authenticate/validate headers and resource bounds before allocating or decompressing.

**Reference semantics.** Every ObjectId-bearing edge declares a wire tag: `StrongRef{oid}` (always followed); `StrongMarkerRef{marker_ref}` and `StrongCommandRef{command_ref}` (retain the named history object); `ConditionalCoordinateRef{oid,graph,branch}` (sequence-neutral payload whose retention sequence comes from its enclosing committed marker); `ConditionalMarkerRef{marker_ref,axis:Global|Branch(graph,branch)}` and `ConditionalCommandRef{command_ref,axis:Logical}` (followed until an authenticated matching checkpoint/cut); `WeakMarkerIdentity{marker_oid,commit_seq}` (provenance/identity only); `WeakLocator`/`PhysicalRealizationRef` (nonretaining local lookup metadata); or `WeakDigest{digest}` (comparison only). Bare `MarkerRef{marker_oid:[u8;32],commit_seq:u64}` and `CommandRef{command_record_oid:[u8;32],logical_command_seq:u64}` are identities, **not reachability by themselves**; an enclosing tag supplies that. `StrongCommandRef` always means a previously constructed `LogicalCommandRecord`; an applied result cites its already identified input and assigned order only through the exact closed `AppliedControlRef`, `AppliedAbortRef`, or `AuthorityAppliedRef` tags below, never an ambient/local-only assumption.

`RemoteObjectIdentity {authority_group_id,object_oid,object_kind,canonical_digest}` is comparison-only and never a local reachability edge. `RemoteAuthorityConfigurationEvidence` is the nonrecursive imported leaf `{database_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,authority_group_role,authority_group_id,configuration_oid,configuration_canonical_digest,canonical_configuration_bytes,configuration_adoption_raft_index,adoption_log_prefix_digest,member_key_set,payload_predicate_digest,trust_transition:Genesis{sharded_genesis_or_raft_role_transition_certificate_digest,configured_genesis_authority_signatures}|Successor{predecessor_evidence_ref:StrongRef<RemoteAuthorityConfigurationEvidence>,joint_transition_transcript,old_configuration_quorum_signatures,new_configuration_quorum_signatures,final_retirement_floor_digest}|ValidatedCheckpointSuccessor{predecessor_anchor_ref:StrongRef<ValidatedRemoteConfigurationAnchor>,joint_transition_transcript,old_configuration_quorum_signatures,new_configuration_quorum_signatures,final_retirement_floor_digest},minimum_configuration_retention_floor,signer_epoch,configuration_quorum_signatures}`. Current-member signatures alone are never a trust root. The embedded exact canonical bytes recompute the OID/digest and self-bind database/role/group; the transition proves adoption from an already trusted genesis or predecessor. Trust-chain compaction uses only the exact input/result protocol below; no inline applied reference or self-signed current checkpoint is a substitute. The authority's own configuration/floor retains canonical bytes, but imported evidence contains no ordinary strong edge back into that group. `RemoteConfigurationRef` means a consumer-local `StrongRef<RemoteAuthorityConfigurationEvidence>`. `RemotePayloadAvailabilityEvidence` is another imported leaf `{authority_configuration_evidence_ref:RemoteConfigurationRef,certificate_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,target_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,target_closure_inventory_digest,payload_predicate_digest,receipt_set_commitment,encoding_placement_coverage,failure_domains,authority_retention_floor,signer_epoch,authority_quorum_signatures}`; the authority ledger separately roots the real certificate/receipts. These signed leaf forms are the only bootstrap exceptions and cannot retain or be followed into the remote object graph.

W12 adds one explicit cross-consensus edge, never disguised as a local `StrongRef`: `CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<T> {authority_group_id,authority_configuration_evidence_ref:RemoteConfigurationRef,consumer_group_id,target_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,target_closure_inventory_digest,payload_availability_evidence_ref:StrongRef<RemotePayloadAvailabilityEvidence>,retention_grant_evidence_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionGrantEvidence>,signer_epoch,quorum_signatures}`. Every `StrongRef` inside the wrapper targets a complete consumer-local leaf-evidence object; none targets an authority-local record. `RemoteRetentionGrantSpec` is authority-group input `{grant_id,authority_group_id,authority_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,consumer_group_id,target_ref:StrongRef,target_kind,target_canonical_digest,target_closure_inventory_digest,payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>,minimum_authority_checkpoint_floor,grant_nonce}`. Authority apply creates the active-only `RemoteRetentionGrantRecord {spec_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionGrantSpec>,authority_applied_ref:AuthorityAppliedRef,state:Active}` in `RemoteRetentionObligationRoot`, which roots the exact target closure. Its quorum then signs the export leaf `RemoteRetentionGrantEvidence {authority_configuration_evidence_ref:RemoteConfigurationRef,grant_record_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,grant_id,consumer_group_id,target_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,target_closure_inventory_digest,payload_availability_evidence_ref:StrongRef<RemotePayloadAvailabilityEvidence>,authority_order_index,minimum_authority_checkpoint_floor,grant_nonce,signer_epoch,authority_quorum_signatures}`. The consumer may publish the remote reference only after importing/authenticating this complete leaf and byte-matching every wrapper field; the authority ledger, not the evidence, owns the target.

Release is an explicit six-transition handshake, never inferred from time or a missing client. (1) After canonically removing/replacing every reference while retaining the grant leaf, the consumer orders `RemoteRetentionReleaseRequestSpec {grant_evidence_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionGrantEvidence>,consumer_release_state_identity:WeakDigest,consumer_checkpoint_floor,successor_grant_evidence_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionGrantEvidence>?,release_nonce}`; apply constructs `RemoteRetentionReleaseRequestRecord {spec_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionReleaseRequestSpec>,consumer_applied_ref:AuthorityAppliedRef,consumer_no_reference_floor_digest}` and installs `ReleaseRequested`. (2) Only afterward does its quorum sign the export leaf `CertifiedRemoteReleaseRequestEvidence {consumer_configuration_evidence_ref:RemoteConfigurationRef,request_record_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,grant_id,authority_group_id,consumer_no_reference_floor_digest,successor_grant_identity?,release_nonce,consumer_order_index,signer_epoch,consumer_quorum_signatures}`; a later publish control installs `ReleaseCertified`, so no future certificate appears in the first result root. (3) The authority imports that leaf and orders `RemoteRetentionReleaseApplySpec {active_grant_record_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionGrantRecord>,release_request_evidence_ref:StrongRef<CertifiedRemoteReleaseRequestEvidence>,expected_active_grant_digest,verified_consumer_no_reference_floor,successor_transfer_proof?}`. Apply rechecks every stronger root, removes the active grant from the authority ownership map, and creates `RemoteRetentionReleaseTombstone {grant_record_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,grant_spec_digest:WeakDigest,target_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,request_evidence_digest:WeakDigest,release_nonce,authority_command_input_digest:WeakDigest,authority_order_index}`; it has no strong edge to the active record, spec, target, or apply command. The release command/log temporarily retains those inputs only until its verified history cut. (4) Only after that applied root does the authority quorum sign leaf `CertifiedRemoteReleaseAckEvidence {authority_configuration_evidence_ref:RemoteConfigurationRef,tombstone_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,grant_id,consumer_group_id,target_identity:RemoteObjectIdentity,release_nonce,authority_order_index,authority_state_root_digest,signer_epoch,authority_quorum_signatures}`. (5) A later authority publish control installs/export-roots that ack evidence. (6) The consumer imports it, orders `ConsumeReleaseAck`, and only then retires request/grant evidence after its checkpoint floor. `AuthorityAppliedRef = Local{command_ref:StrongRef<ControlCommand>,logical_command_seq}|Meta{command_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlCommand>,global_logical_command_seq}|Shard{command_ref:StrongRef<ShardControlCommand>,shard_raft_index}` is used only inside its owning group and prevents role ambiguity. A crash at any handshake point leaves an authority target root or a replayable pending transition; no imported leaf contains an ordinary strong edge into its source group.

W12 history wrappers are distinct rather than overloading the local `LogicalCommandRecord` tag: `StrongGlobalCommandRef{record_oid,global_logical_command_seq}`, `ConditionalGlobalCommandRef{record_oid,global_logical_command_seq,axis=GlobalLogical}`, and `WeakGlobalCommandIdentity{record_oid,global_logical_command_seq}` target `GlobalTxnRecord|GlobalControlRecord`; `ConditionalGlobalTxnInputRef{command_oid,assigned_global_logical_command_seq,axis=GlobalLogical}` targets the already-built `GlobalTxnCommand` and is valid only when the record at that sequence names the same input; `StrongShardCommandRef{record_oid,shard_id,shard_raft_index}`, `ConditionalShardCommandRef{record_oid,shard_id,shard_raft_index,axis=ShardRaft}`, and `WeakShardCommandIdentity{record_oid,shard_id,shard_raft_index}` target `ShardCommandRecord`. Strong variants retain, conditional variants stop only at a verified matching meta/shard checkpoint cut, and weak variants compare only. Cross-group carriage of any target still requires `CertifiedRemoteStrongRef`; these wrappers are only within the owning consensus group.

Canonical result objects that can be produced in either posture use closed role tags rather than pretending every input is local: `AppliedControlRef = Local{command_ref:StrongRef<ControlCommand>,logical_command_seq} | Meta{command_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlCommand>,global_logical_command_seq}`; `AppliedAbortRef = LocalControl{command_ref:StrongRef<ControlCommand>,logical_command_seq} | MetaControl{command_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlCommand>,global_logical_command_seq} | MetaTxn{command_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnCommand>,global_logical_command_seq}`; and `AuditCandidateRef = Local{blocked_after_logical_command_seq,candidate_state_root_ref:StrongRef<LogicalStateRoot>} | Meta{blocked_after_global_logical_command_seq,candidate_state_root_ref:StrongRef<GlobalStateRoot>}`. The group-role validator accepts only the matching tag. These tags are part of the v1 durable schema and the generated spec/result compatibility matrix; no decoder infers posture from ambient configuration.

Key-envelope openers use the separate retaining physical edge `StrongCiphertextRef { logical_oid, ciphertext_id, dek_id, ciphertext_digest, protected_length, key_opener_ref:StrongRef, recoverability_profile, selected_realizations[{encoding_id,placement_id,failure_domain_set}],payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef }`. Its target ciphertext, complete authenticated realization inventory, and certificate exist before the referring envelope object, and the certificate must prove that the selected set satisfies the named profile under the exact configuration. It pins that `CiphertextId` and the selected recoverable `EncodingId`/`PlacementId` set; recoding or movement first creates a successor envelope/grant edge with a newly certified set before the old set can retire, while re-encryption cannot substitute a new ciphertext under a live reference. This is intentionally stronger than ordinary logical reachability and is included in GC, reconfiguration, backup, and key-destruction floors.

For compactness in the schemas below, an otherwise unannotated field ending in `_oid`, `_root`, `_ref`, or an ObjectId-valued collection element is encoded as `StrongRef`; a field ending in `_digest` is comparison-only `WeakDigest` unless an explicit wrapper says otherwise. Bootstrap-slot root identity is an external GC root and is followed as strong. Pending/prepared traversal treats `ConditionalCoordinateRef` as strong because no committed-marker cut context exists. Archive identities are a separate nonlocal type defined below and can never enter the local ObjectId mark set. Every strong/currently-followed-conditional field carries a generated `PriorObject` construction annotation: its concrete target bytes and full identity must exist before the parent encoder runs. Recursive persistent nodes are legal only in that child-before-parent direction. A generated schema/reference/DAG checker compares every field below with Rust encoders and registry rows, rejects unresolved/self/mutual/future-result cycles in reachable instances, and fails G0 on drift. Unknown tags/context fail closed.

**RootSlot + RootBootstrap.** Each slot is exactly 4096 bytes at offsets 0 and 4096:

```text
RootSlot {
  magic="FGRT", format_major:u16, format_minor:u16, slot_generation:u64,
  local_writer_fence_epoch:u64, database_id:[u8;16],
  database_security_namespace_id:[u8;32], cluster_incarnation:u64,
  root_manifest_oid:[u8;32],
  bootstrap: RootBootstrap, reserved_zeroes, tear_checksum:[u8;32]
}
RootBootstrap {
  root_encoding_id:[u8;32], root_placement_id:[u8;32],
  root_placement_epoch:u64, failure_domain_policy_id:[u8;32],
  root_failure_domain_id:[u8;32], segment_id:[u8;16], offset:u64,
  encoded_len:u64, root_symbol_inventory_digest:[u8;32],
  object_kind:u16, canonical_plaintext_len:u64, codec_profile:u32,
  compressed_len:u64, data_crypto_profile:u32, dek_id:[u8;32],
  nonce_len:u8, nonce_or_siv:[u8;32], object_tag_len:u8,
  fec_profile:u32, transfer_length:u64, oti_common:u64, oti_scheme:u32,
  symbol_size:u32, source_block_count:u32, symbol_auth_profile:u16,
  ciphertext_id:[u8;32], ciphertext_digest:[u8;32], opener_kind:u16,
  oid_key_id:[u8;32], opener_payload_len:u16, opener_payload:[u8;1024],
  opener_digest:[u8;32]
}
```

Unused nonce/opener bytes are zero. Profile registries fix bounds and tag lengths. Together with `root_manifest_oid`, these fields reproduce the root's exact `CipherDescriptorWithoutDigest`, complete `EncodingDescriptorWithoutId`, and specialized `PlacementDescriptorWithoutId { encoding_id, root_placement_epoch, failure_domain_policy_id, ContiguousSpan { root_failure_domain_id, segment_id, offset, encoded_len, root_symbol_inventory_digest } }` byte-for-byte. Recovery scans the declared span, authenticates canonical SymbolRecords, verifies the sorted inventory commitment, and recomputes `root_placement_id` before decode. `opener_payload` is a versioned bundle of inline wraps or authenticated KMS/HSM locators sufficient to recover both the named root DEK and immutable `K_oid` without consulting the object index; its digest covers kind, key IDs, locators/wraps, and namespace/incarnation. The authenticated root repeats the exact database/security-namespace/incarnation tuple, and recovery rejects disagreement before following its closure. A structurally valid highest-generation slot is never silently rolled back after authentication/closure failure (§5.1).

**Filesystem durability and writer takeover.** `FilesystemDurabilityProfile` is a signed/checked-in artifact `{ profile_id, profile_version, os/kernel_range, allowed_filesystems_and_mount_predicates, forbidden_layers/options, required_lock_primitive, owner_death_rule, stable_inode_rule, slot_write_rule, file_sync_rule, directory_sync_rule, rename_no_replace_rule, cache_flush_assumption, probe_suite_oid }`. `FGFS-LINUX-LOCAL-V1` has exactly §5.1's ext4/XFS allowlist; a profile/mount not matching every predicate is not writable. A local `FilesystemInstanceRecord { profile_id, probe_suite_oid, mount_id, filesystem_type, canonical_mount_options, device_chain_digest, directory_device_inode, manifest_device_inode, checked_at, result_digest }` is diagnostic evidence, never a transferable proof or semantic root.

The takeover checker accepts only `NoGuard -> LeaseHeld(identity) -> ClosureRecovered(old_epoch) -> PendingFenceGuard(old_epoch+1) -> FenceRootDurableAndReread(old_epoch+1) -> WriterEnabled(FenceToken)`. Creation is `NoGuard -> StagingInodeLease -> PendingCreationGuard(epoch=1) -> CompleteStagingRootVerified -> RenameNoReplaceAndDirectorySync -> CanonicalRootReread -> WriterEnabled`. `PendingFenceGuard` is linear and can encode/seal exactly one fence-only `RootManifest` preserving the recovered state plus its inactive `RootSlot`; `PendingCreationGuard` can encode/seal only the registered Genesis closure and epoch-1 slot. Neither type implements user-segment, prepared-owner, receipt, Raft, canonical-transition, or general-root traits. `FenceToken` is nonserializable and nonconstructible outside the VFS/commit boundary; it binds the live lease handle, stable directory/root identity, profile, slot generation, and epoch. The fence-only root/slot must retain the exact prior canonical logical root, Raft/audit candidate, prepared root, and durable/applied/visible positions. Every immutable segment trailer records `{ database_security_namespace_id, cluster_incarnation, local_writer_fence_epoch, segment_id, sealed_len, inventory_digest, trailer_checksum }`; after promotion the local VFS refuses a seal, prepared-root update, receipt signature, Raft append acknowledgement/proposal, or root publication without the matching live token. Already receipted/ordered records from an older epoch remain strong obligations but cannot authorize new old-epoch publication. The crash matrix cuts after every lease/identity/recovery/object-sync/slot-write/slot-sync/staging-rename/directory-sync/reread step and includes owner death, path replacement, mount drift, stale descriptors, epoch overflow, competing creators, orphan staging, and a lying-sync profile that must be rejected.

**Cipher/encoding/placement records and SymbolRecord.** `CipherDescriptorWithoutDigest` is `{ logical_oid, object_kind, canonical_plaintext_len, codec_profile, compressed_len, data_crypto_profile, dek_id, object_nonce_or_siv, object_tag_len }`. Object AAD is the domain string plus logical OID and this canonical descriptor. `CiphertextRecord` is `{ descriptor, ciphertext_id, ciphertext_digest, object_tag_digest, protected_length }`; `CiphertextId` hashes descriptor+ciphertext+object tag. Immutable `EncodingDescriptorWithoutId` is `{ ciphertext_id, fec_profile, transfer_length, oti_common, oti_scheme, symbol_size, source_block_count, symbol_auth_profile }`, and `EncodingId` hashes the domain/version plus its **complete canonical bytes**. Separately, `PlacementDescriptorWithoutId` is `{ encoding_id, placement_epoch, failure_domain_policy, location_form }`, where `location_form = ContiguousSpan{failure_domain_id,segment_id,offset,encoded_len,symbol_inventory_digest} | Explicit{sorted_symbol_inventory_and_locators,failure_domains}`. `PlacementId` hashes the placement domain/version plus exactly that descriptor; immutable `PlacementRecord { placement_id, descriptor }` merely stores and cross-checks it. Moving/adding symbols creates a new placement record without changing encoding identity. KEK/wrap epoch is absent from both ciphertext and encoding identity. The authenticated local physical-realization index maps `CiphertextId`, `EncodingId`, and `PlacementId` to these records with nonretaining locators. An ordinary decoder obtains the complete descriptor/OTI/auth profile from an authenticated `EncodingDescriptorWithoutId` (or FGP's authenticated encoding prelude) before accepting any symbol; a bare `SymbolRecord` is never self-authorizing.

```text
SymbolRecord {
  magic="FGEC", format_version:u16, header_len:u16, record_len:u32,
  logical_oid:[u8;32], ciphertext_id:[u8;32], encoding_id:[u8;32],
  object_kind:u16, source_block:u32, esi:u32, symbol_len:u32,
  transfer_length:u64, oti_common:u64, oti_scheme:u32, flags:u32,
  symbol_mac_profile:u16, symbol_mac_len:u16,
  payload:[u8;symbol_len], symbol_mac:[u8;symbol_mac_len]
}
```

The symbol MAC key/transcript are exactly §5.1's domain-separated construction. All framing/OTI/length fields and payload are MACed. Truncated/noncanonical tails are ignored only in proved-unreferenced staging; a reachable sealed tail triggers authenticated repair or fail-closed recovery.
