`Commit{routing_certificate_ref:StrongRef<ParticipantRoutingCertificate>,participant_prepare_certificate_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardPrepareCertificate>],distributed_serialization_certificate_ref:StrongRef<DistributedSerializationCertificate>,constraint_reservation_refs[ConstraintReservationRef],global_authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<GlobalAuthorizationDecisionRecord>,resource_transition_refs[StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>],global_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnOutcomePreparationRecord>,terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate,expected_global_commit_seq,expected_branch_heads[WeakMarkerIdentity],expected_branch_key_epochs,global_final_effect_digest}` requires exact admission equality, one valid prepare for every admitted participant, the complete reservation set, and byte-equality across every serialization/auth/resource/outcome/audit field. `AbortAfterAdmission{stable_reason,no_effect_proof_ref:StrongRef,known_prepare_certificate_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardPrepareCertificate>],known_remote_constraint_reservation_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<GlobalConstraintReservationCertificate>],meta_constraint_reservation_refs[StrongRef<MetaConstraintReservationRecord>],abort_authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>,resource_release_refs[StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>],global_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnOutcomePreparationRecord>,terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate,expected_conflict_index_basis:WeakStateIdentity}` is constructible from the published admission plus pre-order no-effect/authorization/release/audit evidence even if no participant prepared; known certificates are retained only for deterministic release. It adopts no effects, creates no marker/delta, releases every meta reservation, and terminalizes conflict/attempt/outcome state. Shard abort acknowledgements necessarily arise only after decision -> certificate publication -> shard apply; they gate client completion, attempt compaction, remote-retention release, and GC, never construction/admission of this abort command. Active-but-unadmitted cancellation is exclusively `GlobalAttemptCancelSpec`, so the two abort paths cannot race.

Meta transaction apply always assigns the next global logical sequence/HLC; only commit also assigns the next global commit sequence. Commit builds the tagged-global `CommitMarker`, atomic head updates, terminal outcome, consumed constraint state, and `GlobalStatePayload`; abort builds the terminal outcome, released constraint state, and payload without marker/effect. Apply then constructs `GlobalTxnRecord` and `GlobalStateRoot`; it does **not** invent future shard batches. `GlobalDecisionCertificate` is built only afterward and quorum-signs `{global_txn_record_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnRecord>,resulting_global_state_root_ref:StrongRef<GlobalStateRoot>,prepare_admission_record_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlRecord>,admission_generation,exact_admitted_participant_set,meta_term/index/configuration,assigned sequences/HLC,decision,marker/effect digest,topology_epoch,retention_floor}`. Certificate formation uses the registered unique aggregate-signature profile or the canonical lowest-ID threshold signer set with deterministic signatures; every signer durably ledgers the identical transcript before release. Until publication the exact bytes are owned by the quorum-durable `MetaCertificateLedger`. `GlobalDecisionCertificatePublishSpec {decision_certificate_ref:StrongRef<GlobalDecisionCertificate>,expected_global_txn_record:WeakDigest,expected_resulting_root:WeakStateIdentity,terminal_audit_gate}` is then ordered as a global control command and installs the certificate in `global_decision_certificate_registry_root`; only that published certificate may be exported as a certified-remote decision. Recovery fetches and verifies the exact ledgered bytes from the retained decision configuration; it never invents a semantically equivalent certificate identity with a different signer set.

`ShardAbortTombstone` is `{prepare_key,prepare_admission_record_ref,decision_certificate_ref,decision_publish_record_ref,shard_id,topology_epoch,applied_shard_raft_index,global_abort_logical_command_seq,state:TerminalAbort}`. `ShardDecisionApplyCommand` is `{decision_certificate_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<GlobalDecisionCertificate>,decision_publish_record_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<GlobalControlRecord>,prepare_key,expected_prepare_record_ref?,expected_absent_or_matching_abort_tombstone,expected_prior_global_applied_logical_command_seq,exact_decision_global_logical_command_seq,expected_topology_epoch,shard_pre_command_base_availability_certificate_ref}`. Its D1 certificate uses the exact current domain/config/predicate and complete decision/publish plus prior-state closure. Commit requires Prepared; abort accepts Prepared or proven absence and installs the terminal tombstone when absent. At global decision `N`, deterministic apply consumes/releases reservations, materializes hidden fragment effects/batch for commit, creates the terminal decision-install state, and advances only `N-1 -> N`; it never jumps through the later Meta audit mirror or certificate-publication control. The resulting `ShardDecisionInstallRecord`/root is durable but not yet a visibility acknowledgement.

The shard must next apply the exact audit-mirror `MetaControlProjectionCertificate` at `N+1` (and any preceding required control in order). Only that projection can make `audit_visible_global_prefix >= N`. From the post-mirror root, the quorum creates `ShardAppliedAck {SameGroupCertificateHeader,decision_certificate_identity,decision_publish_record_identity,audit_mirror_record_identity,prepare_key,terminal_result:Prepared{terminal_prepare_record_ref}|NoPrepare{abort_tombstone_ref},resulting_post_mirror_shard_state_root_ref:StrongRef<ShardLogicalStateRoot>,fragment_batch_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaBatch>?,global_applied_logical_command_seq>=N+1,decision_global_logical_command_seq:N,global_applied_commit_seq,local_raft_index,audit_visible_prefix>=N,shard_payload_floor_ref,quorum_signatures}`. No pre-mirror ack is exportable. Meta publishes this typed ack in its directory and requires one from every admitted participant before global delta construction, client completion, attempt compaction, remote release, or GC. Retry reproduces the same terminal commitment; decision install never bypasses the audit mirror.

After every committed participant has produced its batch and acknowledgement, meta constructs `GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch {global_txn_record_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnRecord>,marker_identity:WeakMarkerIdentity,global_commit_seq,sorted_fragment_batches[{shard_id,fragment_batch_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<LogicalDeltaBatch>,fragment_digest}],sorted_apply_ack_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardAppliedAck>],complete_participant_commitment,resulting_global_frontier,batch_digest}`. The already-known transaction record points to no batch, so the object graph is acyclic. `GlobalDeltaPublishSpec {global_batch_ref:StrongRef<GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch>,expected_prior_global_frontier,expected_transaction_and_marker:WeakDigest,terminal_audit_gate}` is a `GlobalControlCommand`; apply verifies exact prepare-set equality and contiguous frontier, then atomically installs the batch/index/frontier through payload→control-record→root. Ripple and client commit acknowledgement wait for this publication, every touched shard durability/apply quorum, terminal audit visibility, and durable outcome; a crash before them yields capability-scoped `Unknown`, never partial delta visibility.

`ShardCheckpointInstallSpec` is `{basis_shard_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_shard_raft_index,basis_global_prefix,basis_payload_digest:WeakDigest,basis_projection_digest,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<ShardRecoveryCheckpoint>,checkpoint_state_vector_digest,paired_shard_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ShardConfigPayloadFloor>?,retention_cut_body_ref:StrongRef<RetentionCutBody>?,reset_field_tags[]}`. Genesis requires no body/floor and produces `CheckpointInstalled`; operational replacement requires both, atomically installs the matching provisional cut, applies only registered reset/equivalence transitions, and preserves `Operational`. `ShardInitialFloorInstallSpec` is `{checkpoint_installed_shard_state:WeakStateIdentity,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<ShardRecoveryCheckpoint>,checkpoint_state_vector_digest,initial_shard_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ShardConfigPayloadFloor>,initial_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,expected_shard_raft_index}` and is the sole fresh `CheckpointInstalled -> Operational` transition. Local-to-W12 migration instead uses `ShardProjectionInstallSpec {transition_certificate_ref:CertifiedRoleTransitionRef,local_to_shard_projection_ref:StrongRef<LocalToShardProjection>,expected_empty_shard_genesis,installed_operational_checkpoint/floor refs,expected_shard_raft_index,expected_global_prefix}` as the one special `Genesis -> Operational` transition; it emits `ShardOperationalBootstrapBarrier` whose fields must equal the transition certificate's precommitted predicate, and is invalid for an ordinary fresh shard. `ShardHistoryCutActivationSpec` is `{provisional_cut_ref:StrongRef<ProvisionalRetentionCutSet>,checkpoint_install_record_ref:StrongShardCommandRef,expected_retention_basis:WeakStateIdentity,verified_contiguous_suffix_start}` and only strengthens the exact provisional set.

`ShardConfigurationTransitionSpec` is `{phase:ProposeJoint|CommitJoint|CommitNew|CommitRetirementFloor,basis_shard_state:WeakStateIdentity,current_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,prospective_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,candidate_closure_proof_ref:StrongRef,expected_shard_raft_index,expected_global_prefix,paired_checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<ShardRecoveryCheckpoint>?,paired_floor_ref:StrongRef<ShardConfigPayloadFloor>,meta_authorization_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardReconfigurationAuthorizationRecord>,prepared_ownership_transfer_refs[StrongRef<PreparedOwnershipTransferRecord>]}`; every field byte-matches the meta authorization, and final apply enables the adoption evidence but does not mutate meta topology. `ShardTopologyCopyApplySpec` is `{copy_record_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<TopologyTransitionRecord>,transfer_plan_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<TopologyTransferPlan>,source_checkpoint_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardCheckpointCertificate>],received_inventory_digest,expected_destination_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,through_global_prefix}`. `ShardDerivedBuildSpec` and `ShardDerivedAdvanceSpec` bind the exact `DerivedIdentity`, input `GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch` CRSR interval, active meta projection, topology/config, prior component, result component root, answer contract, and availability floor; apply roots the component before a certificate is exported. `ShardKeyMaterialProjectionSpec` binds the exact meta manifest/projection CRSR, current topology/config, expected prior registry entry, and complete local envelope/wrap/opener availability. These typed controls, not a generic payload import, are the only derived/key installation paths.

`MetaControlProjectionCertificate` is the meta-quorum-signed `{SameGroupCertificateHeader,source_global_control_record_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlRecord>,source_global_command_kind,target_shard_id,before_global_prefix,after_global_prefix,topology_before/after:StrongRef<TopologyState>,policy_epoch_before/after,revocation_index_before/after,key_epoch_commitment_before/after,audit_visibility_before/after,required_remote_payload_refs[StrongRef],projection_checker_version,quorum_signatures}`. It is valid only for a published relevant control, commits every shard-visible security/routing/key/audit consequence, and cannot summarize transaction effects or a range. `ShardMetaControlApplySpec` is `{projection_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<MetaControlProjectionCertificate>,expected_shard_state:WeakStateIdentity,expected_prior_global_prefix,required_imported_payload_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef],expected_topology_epoch,expected_policy_epoch,expected_revocation_index,expected_key_epoch_commitment,expected_audit_visibility_prefix}`. Apply verifies the exact next global command, imports all named payloads under two-sided retention, updates `ActiveMetaProjectionRoot`, and advances exactly one contiguous durable prefix. Audit visibility may remain fixed behind a fence but can never decrease; only the exact mirror projection advances it, and `after_visible < before_visible` is invalid.

`ShardControlCommand` is the fence-free envelope `{command_version,kind,body:AdvanceIrrelevantRange{proof_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<MetaRelevanceRangeProof>}|ApplyMetaControl{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardMetaControlApplySpec>}|RemoteRetention{spec_ref:StrongRef<RemoteRetentionControlSpec>}|ValidateRemoteConfigurationAnchor{spec_ref:StrongRef<ValidateRemoteConfigurationAnchorSpec>}|InstallCheckpoint{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardCheckpointInstallSpec>}|InstallInitialFloor{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardInitialFloorInstallSpec>}|InstallMigrationProjection{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardProjectionInstallSpec>}|ActivateHistoryCut{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardHistoryCutActivationSpec>}|ConfigurationTransition{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardConfigurationTransitionSpec>}|GcPreflight{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardGcPreflightSpec>}|GcApply{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardGcApplySpec>}|DerivedBuild{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardDerivedBuildSpec>}|DerivedAdvance{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardDerivedAdvanceSpec>}|InstallKeyMaterial{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardKeyMaterialProjectionSpec>}|TopologyCopyApply{spec_ref:StrongRef<ShardTopologyCopyApplySpec>},expected_shard_raft_index,expected_state_conditions[],shard_pre_command_base_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<ShardPreCommandBaseAvailabilityCertificate>}`. The certificate/owner identity must match this exact control body and configuration before proposal. It cannot change global semantic values. `AdvanceIrrelevantRange` is legal only for an exhaustive `MetaRelevanceRangeProof`; topology, policy, revocation, key, audit-fence, admission/decision, remote-retention, derived activation, or target-data effects require their typed apply path and can never be skipped. `audit_visible_global_prefix` never decreases: a fence may hold it unchanged while durable apply advances, and only the exact mirror projection advances it. Any projection with `after_visible < before_visible` is invalid. Never-registered and closed-attempt compaction powers are the separate typed floors above; neither a floor nor timeout may terminalize a prepared attempt.

Topology evidence is typed. `TopologyTransferPlan` is `{old_topology_ref,new_joint_topology_ref,new_final_topology_ref,affected_ranges,copy_basis_global_prefix,sorted_source_checkpoint_identities,object_and_suffix_inventory,destination_assignments,copy_crypto_profile,completion_predicate}`. A destination shard produces `TopologyTransferAck {SameGroupCertificateHeader,plan_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<TopologyTransferPlan>,destination_shard,received_inventory_digest,applied_through_global_prefix,destination_checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<ShardCheckpointCertificate>,signatures}`. Meta builds `TopologyAttemptClosureProof {SameGroupCertificateHeader,old_topology_epoch,cutover_global_prefix,registration_generation_range,sorted_attempt_evidence[(global_txn_id,registration_generation) -> Terminal{outcome_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnOutcomeRecord>,published_decision_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlRecord>?,old_owner_ack_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardAppliedAck>]}|AbortForPostCutoverRetry{abort_outcome_ref:StrongRef<GlobalTxnOutcomeRecord>,published_abort_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlRecord>,old_owner_release_ack_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardAppliedAck>],retry_request_nonce,intent_commitment,old_to_future_attempt_mapping_commitment}],exact_old_epoch_active_and_admitted_set_commitment,conflict_index_basis,signatures}`. The sorted evidence is exhaustive against old-epoch attempt indexes. No new-epoch registration can preexist cutover: only a later meta command after ownership switches may create a new generation and link it to the recorded retry intent. A registration racing the cutover basis is either included/terminalized under the old epoch or rejected for later retry. `TopologyRetirementFloor` is `{cutover_record_ref:StrongRef<TopologyTransitionRecord>,through_global_prefix,old_owner_inventory,remaining_certified_remote_obligations,backup_floor,key_floor,retention_floor,prepare_floor,external_backup_and_key_receipt_refs[StrongRef],required_meta_ack_set,required_shard_ack_set}`. `TopologyRetirementAck` carries `SameGroupCertificateHeader` and `{floor_ref:LocalMeta{StrongRef<TopologyRetirementFloor>}|RemoteMeta{CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<TopologyRetirementFloor>},satisfied_floor_digest,signature}`; only meta encodes `LocalMeta`, and every shard encodes `RemoteMeta`.

Movement has three distinct pre-order global-control specs so apply never consumes ambient evidence. `TopologyCopyBeginSpec` is `{move_id,old_topology_ref,new_joint_topology_ref,new_final_topology_ref,affected_ranges,copy_basis_global_prefix,old/new_shard_configuration_refs[RemoteConfigurationRef],source_checkpoint_certificate_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardCheckpointCertificate>],transfer_plan_ref:StrongRef<TopologyTransferPlan>,expected_branch/key/allocation_epochs,terminal_audit_gate}`. `TopologyCutoverSpec` is `{move_id,copy_record_ref:StrongRef<TopologyTransitionRecord>,cutover_global_prefix,sorted_transfer_ack_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<TopologyTransferAck>],new_owner_catchup_certificate_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardCheckpointCertificate>],active_attempt_closure_proof_ref:StrongRef<TopologyAttemptClosureProof>,old/new_shard_configuration_refs[RemoteConfigurationRef],expected_branch/key/allocation_epochs,terminal_audit_gate}` and proves every old-epoch registration has exhaustive Terminal or `AbortForPostCutoverRetry` evidence before ownership switches at the next prefix. `TopologyRetireOldSpec` is `{move_id,cutover_record_ref:StrongRef<TopologyTransitionRecord>,topology_retirement_floor_ref:StrongRef<TopologyRetirementFloor>,sorted_meta_ack_refs[StrongRef<TopologyRetirementAck>],sorted_shard_ack_refs[CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<TopologyRetirementAck>],terminal_audit_gate}`. Each apply constructs one `TopologyTransitionRecord {move_id,phase:CopyInProgress|CutoverCommitted|OldOwnersRetired,command_ref:StrongRef<GlobalControlCommand>,phase_predecessor:NoneForCopy|Copy{ref:StrongRef<TopologyTransitionRecord>}|Cutover{ref:StrongRef<TopologyTransitionRecord>},copy_basis_global_prefix,cutover_global_prefix?,affected_ranges,evidence_commitment,resulting_topology_ref,assigned_global_logical_command_seq}`. The predecessor is the immediately prior same-move phase; completed moves do not form an unbounded strong chain. Source bytes/keys remain live through final retirement and its two-sided remote floors.

**AdjRunSegment**: `{ graph, branch_projection, source_partition, direction, edge_type, source_ordinal_map_id, destination_map_table[{partition,ordinal_map_id}], source_ordinal_range, edge_count, seq_range, codec_table, offsets_ef, encoded_neighbor_lists, stable_eids, origin_birth_orders, branch_admission_orders?, marker_aware_retire_or_hole_data, property_locators, canonical_stable_id_digest, checksum }`. Each destination carries either stable VId or a destination-map-table slot plus ordinal. Mutable labels do not identify a primary run; per-list codec governs legal rank/select/skip operations.

**IdentityContinuityRecord / IdAllocatorState / IdRangeLease**: `IdentityContinuityRecord` binds `{database_security_namespace_id,allocation_epoch,predecessor_digest,external_registry_id,cas_version,status,issued_at,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}`; its external registry/witness copy is the anti-rollback authority and its Chronicle copy is checked against it. Allocator state binds `{graph_id,element_kind,allocation_epoch,identity_continuity_record_ref,topology_epoch,per_partition_high_water,spent_range_commitments,exhausted_partitions}`. Pre-order `IdRangeGrantSpec` binds the requested range, allocator basis, and authority. Its applied lease is `{lease_id,graph,element_kind,allocation_epoch,partition,half_open_range,authority_digest,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef,issuance_not_after,permanent_spent_commitment}`. The applied tag must match the owning local/meta state machine and assigned sequence. Expiry ends issuance authority only; every epoch/range pair remains permanently spent and can never overlap or recycle.

**CommittedEffectCapsule**: `{ read_snapshot_basis, validated_apply_basis, intent_semantics_oid, read_graph_reference_bindings[], validated_write_coordinate_bindings[], validated_write_key_epoch_bindings[{graph,branch,envelope_epoch,write_key_epoch}], coordinate_schema_transitions[], topology_epoch, policy_epoch, revocation_index, effect_directory_root, committed_effect_refs[ConditionalCoordinateRef], constraint_evidence, authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>, authorization_decision_digest:WeakDigest, authorized_permit_scope_digest, resource_transition_refs[StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>], resource_charge_effects, txn_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef<TxnOutcomePreparationRecord>, final_read_witnesses, final_write_summary, birth_ordinals, merge_record_ref:StrongRef<MergeRecord>?, logical_delta_template_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaTemplate>, logical_delta_template_digest:WeakDigest, optional_physical_accelerators[{apply_basis,digest,payload_ref:StrongRef}], txn_token, final_effect_digest }`. The immutable effect directory Merkle-commits coordinate-enveloped payload OIDs but remains sequence-neutral; the owning committed marker supplies retention time. Repeated digests cross-check the strongly referenced bytes and never replace ownership. The referenced template's full ObjectId and bytes must match the digest and final effect set. Role-bearing read bindings preserve repeated historical graph references; role-free write bindings own state transitions. The capsule contains permanent IDs and no unresolved conditional command, ambient input, local writer fence, or stale derived delta. Every new encoding/wrap in its prepared closure must match the exact key-epoch binding; a mismatch is not repairable at apply. The marker produced by apply becomes the resulting head in each transitioned coordinate's next `CoordinateSchemaBinding`; the capsule never self-references that future marker.

**CommitCommand / ControlCommand / LogicalCommandRecord / PreparedCommitRecord.** A transaction order unit is `{command_version,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,txn_token,capsule_ref:StrongRef,logical_delta_template_ref:StrongRef,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef,resource_transition_refs[StrongRef],txn_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef,payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef,expected_logical_command_seq,expected_branch_heads[WeakMarkerIdentity],expected_branch_key_epochs[{graph,branch,envelope_epoch,write_key_epoch}],topology_epoch,policy_epoch,revocation_index,proposed_physical_hlc,final_effect_digest}`. A `ControlCommand` is `{command_version,kind,schema_version,typed_payload_ref:StrongRef<SequenceNeutralSpec>,payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>?,expected_logical_command_seq,expected_state_conditions[WeakStateIdentity|WeakMarkerIdentity|ExpectedEpoch|ExpectedIndex],proposed_physical_hlc,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>,terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate}`; CAS expectations are comparison-only and never retain a prior root. The generated `PayloadBearingControlKind` table requires `Some` for branch fork/grant bundles, remote-retention/config-anchor evidence publication, backup/restore, and any other spec whose closure adds payload bytes; the certificate covers the exact already-built spec/bundle/evidence closure and excludes the future command. Non-payload kinds require `None` unless their registered schema says otherwise.

Every typed sequence-neutral spec is canonically encoded as `{spec_body,terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate}`; inline spec braces elsewhere abbreviate only `spec_body` and never make the gate optional. The local kind registry includes `TxnSubmissionSpec`, `TxnAbortSpec`, `CheckpointInstallSpec`, `InitialConfigFloorInstallSpec`, `HistoryCutActivationSpec`, `RemoteRetentionControlSpec`, `ValidateRemoteConfigurationAnchorSpec`, `IdRangeGrantSpec`, `BranchForkSpec`, `BranchGrantSpec`, `MergePrepareSpec`, `MergeRejectSpec`, `DpTransitionSpec`, `DeliveryLeaseTransitionSpec`, `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec`, `AuditTerminalSpec`, `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec`, `AuditRecoverySpec`, `AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec`, schema/policy/resource/revocation specs, `KeyDestroyProposal`, `KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec`, `GcProposal`, and `ConfigurationTransitionSpec`. Actual committed merge effects use the ordinary transaction `CommitCommand`/capsule/marker path; only token preparation and deterministic pre-effect rejection are control commands. `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec`, `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec`, `AuditRecoverySpec`, and `AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec` are fixed `TerminalAuditGate::StructurallyInapplicable` under `AuditSystemAuthority`; the exact audit admission, terminal, mirror, and completeness bodies are fixed below. Every other state-changing control spec carries the same canonical gate as its command, and apply rejects inequality or a control-mutation event whose kind/spec/expected-condition/transition commitments do not match. No spec may point to its applied result or resulting root. Every transaction or control command deterministically advances `logical_hlc_state` and records that value as `logical_command_hlc`; a transaction additionally copies it to its marker and advances `CommitSeq`. Apply constructs result objects, then `LogicalStatePayload`, then `LogicalCommandRecord {logical_command_seq,predecessor:ConditionalCommandRef{axis=Logical}?,command:StrongRef<CommitCommand|ControlCommand>,transaction_marker:StrongMarkerRef?,logical_command_hlc,resulting_state_payload_digest:WeakDigest}`, then `LogicalStateRoot {payload_ref:StrongRef,logical_command_head:StrongCommandRef?}`; only genesis uses `None`.

Exact local `ConfigurationTransitionSpec` is `{phase:ProposeJoint|CommitJoint|CommitNew|CommitRetirementFloor,basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,current_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,prospective_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,candidate_closure_proof_ref:StrongRef,paired_checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>?,paired_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,required_prepared/certificate/remote/key/audit/backup_obligation_floor,terminal_audit_gate}`; every phase is a separate command and final retirement proves the new configuration owns every obligation. Exact local `GcProposal` is `{basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,retention_map_digest,complete_typed_root_inventory_digest,sorted_reclaim_objects_and_realizations,availability_and_retirement_ack_refs[StrongRef],excluded_live_prepared/certificate/remote/key/backup/legal_hold/replay/audit/capability obligations,terminal_audit_gate}`; follower recomputation must derive the identical set and only its applied `GcDecisionRecord` authorizes retirement.

A replica-local `PreparedCommitRecord` is `{prepared_ownership_id,prepare_id,record_generation,predecessor_ref:StrongRef<PreparedCommitRecord>?,database_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,group_role:Local,group_id,configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,payload_predicate_digest,local_writer_fence_epoch,txn_token,capsule_ref:StrongRef,command_ref:StrongRef?,base_closure_inventory_digest,current_closure_inventory_digest,strong_logical_refs[StrongRef],exact_realizations[{object_or_subobject_id,encoding_id,placement_id,key_opener_ref:StrongRef}],status:Preparing|Receipted|Ordered{raft_index}|Applied{logical_command_seq,commit_seq}|Abandoned{fence_proof_digest},receipt_nonce}`. Recomputing its ownership ID and every receipt transcript includes the exact database/incarnation/Local group/configuration OID and predicate digest. `PreparedPayloadRoot` maps the stable ownership ID to the latest immutable successor. Every successor repeats the same domain/config/predicate/base inventory and has an identical or superset current closure; a receipt commitment is retained. `Receipted`/`Ordered` ownership cannot be removed by timeout or crash; only the fenced terminal rules in §5.2 and a committed GC decision may release it. On apply, ownership transfers to the command record/marker/logical state/outcome index before the prepared entry becomes terminal.

**LogicalDeltaTemplate / LogicalDeltaBatch.** A template is `{ format, intent_semantics_oid, final_effect_digest, source_intent_digest, coordinate_entries[] }`, where entries are canonically sorted and each is `{ graph, branch, relation_id, validated_schema_binding, schema_transition?, delta_payload_ref:ConditionalCoordinateRef, delta_payload_digest }`. The payload is a canonical exact Z-set over `CanonicalRow`; duplicate coordinates/relations, zero weights, noncanonical order, a transition inconsistent with its binding, or a payload not equal to the capsule's before/after effects are invalid. Prepared traversal follows every conditional edge as strong; committed traversal supplies the enclosing marker sequence and may apply only a matching `EffectCut`. A self-contained materialized batch is `{ format, source_template_digest:WeakDigest, commit_marker_identity:WeakMarkerIdentity, commit_seq, coordinate_entries[{source_binding,resulting_binding,relation_id,delta_payload_ref:StrongRef}], global_frontier, batch_digest }`. `batch_digest` covers all preceding canonical fields and is also the batch idempotency key; the object's full ObjectId is `LogicalDeltaBatchId`. Apply/rematerialization must reproduce the same object. A retained batch owns payloads directly but does not retain template, marker, capsule, or predecessor history. Delta-history leases are explicit roots and checkpoint cutting cannot silently invalidate a promised resume range.

**DeliveredBaselinePayload / DeliveredDeltaPayload / DeltaDeliveryEnvelope / resume cursor and lease registry.** `DeliveredBaselinePayload` is `{format,baseline_id,derived_identity_digest,source_coverage,baseline_frontier,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_row_segment_refs[StrongRef],canonical_payload_len,baseline_digest}`; its public digest hashes the domain plus every preceding field and exact concatenated canonical result bytes, not keyed segment IDs. `DeliveredDeltaPayload` is `{format,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_zset_segment_refs[StrongRef],canonical_payload_len,output_payload_digest}` with the analogous public exact-byte digest. `CommittedDeltaSourceRef` is exactly `Local{batch_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaBatch>,commit_seq}|Global{batch_ref:StrongRef<GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch>,global_commit_seq}`. `DeltaDeliveryEnvelope` is `{format,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,tenant_principal_authority_digest,derived_identity_digest,baseline_id,start_frontier,resulting_frontier,output_payload_ref:StrongRef<DeliveredDeltaPayload>,output_payload_digest,provenance:Atomic{source:CommittedDeltaSourceRef,source_batch_digest}|Coalesced{source_role:Local|Global,first_batch_id,last_batch_id,ordered_source_commitment,source_count},delivery_digest}`. Local and Global frontiers/source IDs have distinct wire tags; W12 emits only meta-published Global sources, never shard `LogicalDeltaBatch` fragments, while migrated outstanding leases preserve Local. `DeliveryDigest` hashes every canonical envelope field except itself, so it commits role, output, and provenance; `DeliveryId` is the opaque full keyed envelope ObjectId. `delivery_lease_id`, `resume_cursor_id`, and every successor capability nonce are pre-minted in the input transition spec.

`DeliveryFrontier = Local{commit_seq,batch_frontier}|Global{global_commit_seq,batch_frontier}`. `ResumeCursorRecord` is `{resume_cursor_id,baseline_id,derived_identity_digest,authority_digest,cursor_state_version,current capability generation/nonce/key epoch/expiry/commitment,predecessor capability/request digests?,posture:Local|Global,baseline_state:Pending|Acknowledged with DeliveryFrontier,acknowledged_frontier:DeliveryFrontier?,last_acked_delivery?,outstanding_delivery_lease_id?,status:BaselinePending|Active|PostureTransitionRequired|ResetRequired|Expired,applied logical/global command seq}`. `DeliveryLeaseRecord` contains the same posture and exactly `Baseline{payload_ref,digest,DeliveryFrontier}|Delta{envelope_ref,delivery id/digest,DeliveryFrontier}`. Registry uniqueness is unchanged. `DeliveryLeaseTransitionSpec` is `CreateCursorAndBaselineLease|AckBaselineComplete|CreateLease|RotateCapability|AckComplete|PostActivationCursorTransition{expected Local cursor version,proved no outstanding Local lease,projected Local frontier,new Global baseline payload/lease and pre-minted successor capability}|ResetOrExpire`. ACK transitions atomically remove exact leases and retain predecessor/request state for lost-response replay. The posture transition sets `Global` only with a pending Global baseline; no Global delta exists before its ACK, and no coalesced/atomic range crosses roles. A capability authorizes lookup but never retains bytes.

**CommitMarker and physical batching.** A canonical marker is independently hashed:

```text
CommitMarker {
  logical_command_seq:u64, commit_seq:u64,
  effect_source:
    Local { capsule_ref:StrongRef<CommittedEffectCapsule>,
            logical_delta_template_digest:WeakDigest }
    | Global { global_txn_input_ref:ConditionalGlobalTxnInputRef,
               routing_and_participant_commitment:WeakDigest,
               final_effect_digest:WeakDigest,
               aggregate_template_digest:WeakDigest },
  prev_global:ConditionalMarkerRef{axis=Global}?,
  head_updates[{graph,branch,
                expected_previous:ConditionalMarkerRef{axis=Branch(graph,branch)}?}],
  merge_record_oid?, coordinate_schema_transition_digest,
  topology_epoch, policy_epoch, revocation_index,
  txn_token, commit_hlc,
  final_effect_digest,
  authorization_decision_digest, resource_effect_digest,
  payload_availability_certificate_oid?, flags, chain_hash
}
```

The marker itself is the implicit new head for each update. Its effect-source tag is fixed by posture: local apply uses the already-built capsule/template pair; W12 meta apply uses `ConditionalGlobalTxnInputRef {command_oid,assigned_global_logical_command_seq}` to the already-built transaction input plus routing/participant/effect/template commitments. The later global record at that exact sequence must name the same command. Before a matching global command cut, traversal follows the conditional input into the full prepared closure; afterward the head marker remains valid without permanently resurrecting remote prepare grants or effect bytes. A reader that does not know the required W12 tag rejects it. The marker deliberately does not name the terminal outcome or any future record/fragment/global batch; apply constructs the marker first and later objects may name it, avoiding outcome/distributed-batch cycles. `chain_hash` hashes the prior chain value plus marker bytes excluding `chain_hash`. `MarkerBatch {first_seq,last_seq,previous_batch_digest,entry_directory[{marker_oid,offset,length}],canonical_marker_bytes,mmr_update,checksum}` is only a physical pack; object locations resolve each marker independently.

**RecoveryCheckpoint / CheckpointStateVector / RetentionMap.** A checkpoint is `{basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,covered_basis_logical_command:WeakCommandIdentity?,covered_global_marker:StrongMarkerRef?,covered_command_chain_hash?,covered_marker_chain_hash?,basis_payload_digest:WeakDigest,basis_projection_digest,logical_hlc_state,checkpoint_state_vector_ref:StrongRef<CheckpointStateVector>,nonretaining_predecessor_checkpoint_digest}`; both covered identities/hashes may be absent only for Genesis. The weak command identity and chain/payload/projection commitments authenticate the cut without retaining prior command/spec/checkpoint chains. The vector is generated from the exact versioned payload schema and has one typed entry per field: `CopiedStrong`, `ProjectedSnapshot`, `ResetByCheckpointInstall`, `SelfExcluded`, or the single constrained `InstallProvisionalCut{field_tag=retention_map_root,retention_cut_body_ref,install_input_kind,assigned_order_literal}`. That fifth tag is required exactly once for an operational basis and forbidden for Genesis; it commits the pre-order body and deterministic applied-result recipe without a future result OID. `recovery_checkpoint_ref` always uses `InstallThisCheckpoint`; operational `config_payload_floor_ref` uses `InstallPairedConfigFloor`, while Genesis copies absence. `basis_projection_digest = BLAKE3("fgdb:checkpoint-projection:v1" ‖ canonical(vector reconstruction with exact literals))`; it never hashes a future checkpoint/floor/cut OID. A missing, duplicate, illegally self-excluded, or otherwise unclassified field is invalid.

`CheckpointInstallSpec` is `{basis:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_payload_digest:WeakDigest,basis_projection_digest,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,checkpoint_state_vector_digest,paired_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>?,retention_cut_body_ref:StrongRef<RetentionCutBody>?,reset_field_tags[]}`. It must be the first retained record at `basis_logical_command_seq+1`; apply verifies the exact current basis/vector, installs its own already-known checkpoint ref, and, for every operational basis, atomically installs the required paired floor and deterministic provisional cut whose checkpoint/vector/prefix and weak observations match. `retention_cut_body_ref=None` is legal only for Genesis, where no prior absence needs re-attestation. Genesis advances to `CheckpointInstalled`; later installs preserve `Operational`, apply only declared resets, and otherwise preserve every field. `InitialConfigFloorInstallSpec {checkpoint_installed_state:WeakStateIdentity,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,checkpoint_state_vector_digest,initial_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,initial_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,expected_logical_command_seq,terminal_audit_gate}` is the sole local `CheckpointInstalled -> Operational` transition.

The closed cut union is `CommandCut {axis:Logical,stop_at:WeakCommandIdentity,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>} | GlobalCommandCut {axis:GlobalLogical,stop_at:WeakGlobalCommandIdentity,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<GlobalRecoveryCheckpoint>,exact_covered_global_prefix} | ShardCommandCut {axis:ShardRaft,stop_at:WeakShardCommandIdentity,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<ShardRecoveryCheckpoint>,exact_covered_shard_raft_index,exact_covered_global_prefix} | MarkerCut {axis,stop_at:WeakMarkerIdentity,checkpoint_ref} | EffectCut {graph,branch,through_seq,effect_payload_digest_range,checkpoint_ref}`. `RetentionCutBody` is the pre-order object `{role:Local|Meta|Shard{shard_id},checkpoint_identity,command_cut,sorted_marker_cuts[],sorted_effect_cuts[],covered_policy_epoch,covered_coordinate_set_commitment,verified_first_retained_order,completeness_digest}` and must contain the role's one command cut plus every marker/effect cut superseded by that checkpoint. The checkpoint-install command strongly owns this body before order. Apply deterministically constructs `ProvisionalRetentionCutSet {body_ref:StrongRef<RetentionCutBody>,install_input_ref:Local{StrongRef<ControlCommand>,assigned_logical_command_seq}|Meta{StrongRef<GlobalControlCommand>,assigned_global_logical_command_seq}|Shard{StrongRef<ShardControlCommand>,assigned_shard_raft_index},basis_projection_digest:WeakDigest}` before constructing the payload. Its input reference, assigned order, and projection digest are already known; the outer state root and command head prove the corresponding applied record. `InstallProvisionalCut` in the vector is an exact literal for this construction.

`HistoryCutActivationSpec {provisional_cut_ref:StrongRef<ProvisionalRetentionCutSet>,checkpoint_install_record_ref:StrongCommandRef,expected_retention_map_basis:WeakStateIdentity,verified_contiguous_suffix_start,terminal_audit_gate}` is the sole local strengthening path; Global/Shard use the matching global/shard record tags. Apply creates `ActivatedRetentionCutSet {provisional_cut_ref:StrongRef<ProvisionalRetentionCutSet>,checkpoint_install_record_ref:StrongCommandRef|StrongGlobalCommandRef|StrongShardCommandRef,activation_applied_ref:AuthorityAppliedRef}` and atomically replaces that provisional map entry. `RetentionMap` contains policy epochs and exactly one `Provisional|Activated` entry for each retained cut body. Operational checkpoint reset atomically drops superseded entries and installs the new provisional set; at every crash point, either the old activated authority or the new provisional authority authenticates already-missing bytes. Traversal may stop only when axis/group/checkpoint/body completeness and the provisional input+assigned-order or activated record proof all validate. Strong roots always win. A cut transfers authority to checkpoint+install+suffix; it does not assert that pruned capsules or old delta ranges remain individually recoverable. Recovery/crash tests begin with bytes already reclaimed under the prior cut and interrupt every install/activation step for all three roles.

**ConstraintState / ResourceLedger / TxnOutcome.** `ConstraintStateRoot` is keyed by a full `CoordinateSchemaBinding` and contains canonical constraint maps plus base-state digest. `ResourceLedgerState` maps tenant/scope to limits, committed charges, and `ResourceReservationId`; `ResourceChargeEffect` atomically creates/releases named durable charges. `TxnOutcomePreparationRecord` binds `{txn_token,expected_prior_state:Absent|Submitted{state_version,state_digest},proposed_terminal_kind,final_effect_digest,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef,resource_transition_refs[StrongRef],terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate}`. `TxnAbortSpec` is `{txn_token,expected_prior_state:Absent|Submitted{state_version,state_digest},reason_class,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef,terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate,resource_release_refs[StrongRef]}`. For either terminal path, the gate's `Required` event must be the exact transaction mutation or no-effect terminal consistent with these bytes. `TxnOutcomeRecord` binds database security namespace/incarnation, scoped token, tenant/principal/authority digest, issuance/expiry and minimum lookup-retention floor, and `state = Submitted{state_version,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef} | Committed{marker_ref:StrongMarkerRef,final_effect_digest} | Aborted{reason_class,applied_abort_ref:AppliedAbortRef}`, plus the same explicit terminal-audit outcome. The role tag must match the state machine that owns the index. `TxnOutcomeIndex` enforces uniqueness, exact compare-and-transition, matching-terminal idempotency, conflicting-terminal rejection, and expiry-tombstone rules. Optional `TxnSubmissionSpec` creates `Submitted`; otherwise a terminal may transition from `Absent`. Only `TxnAbortSpec` creates the local aborted state; W12 uses the exact global lifecycle record below. A `TxnOutcomeCapability` authenticates lookup/retry of the role-tagged record and never grants mutation authority.

**BranchManifest / branch key-envelope DAG.** A branch manifest is `{graph,branch_id,fork_parent,fork_parent_head:StrongMarkerRef,fork_seq,base_checkpoint_ref?,key_envelope_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,current_envelope_epoch,current_write_key_epoch,policy}`. `WeakEpochIdentity` is `{graph,branch,kind,epoch,record_oid,rotation_chain_digest}` and is nonretaining. `BranchKeyEpochRecord` is the pre-order-buildable `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,graph,branch,kind:Envelope|Write,epoch,key_id,predecessor:Genesis|SameEpochLifecycle{ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>}|PriorEpoch{identity:WeakEpochIdentity},transition_nonce,expected_install_logical_command_seq,state:Active{opened_at_logical_command_seq}|Closed{opened_at_logical_command_seq,closed_through_logical_command_seq,close_reason}}`. Closing an epoch uses the strong same-epoch predecessor because both records describe one key lifecycle; opening a successor uses only the weak prior-epoch identity/rotation-chain commitment. Command history, transparency, and the epoch registry authenticate that rotation without making the current epoch retain every old key forever. It deliberately does not point forward to its installing command. Epoch ordinals, transition nonce, keys, and exact expected install sequence are pre-minted; apply installs the already identified record only when its expected sequence and predecessor commitment equal current state. Old envelope roots/nodes/grants/backups—not a permanent epoch chain—are the strong owners that keep an old key decryptable; when they disappear, two-stage destruction can actually prove zero references.

`KeyEnvelopeNode` is `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,owning_graph,owning_branch,envelope_epoch,node_kind,coverage_cut:{through_logical_command_seq,through_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity?},children[{range,child_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeNode>,child_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,wrapped_child_dek,wrap_profile,aad_bytes,aad_digest}],inherited_roots[{source_graph,source_branch,source_envelope_epoch,source_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,source_root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,maximum_logical_command_seq,maximum_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity?,wrapped_source_envelope_key,wrapped_source_root_dek,wrap_profile,aad_bytes,aad_digest}],write_epochs[{write_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,allowed_creation_range,wrapped_write_epoch_key,wrap_profile,aad_bytes,aad_digest}]}`. `KeyEnvelopeRoot` is `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,graph,branch,envelope_epoch,envelope_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,current_write_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,root_node_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeNode>,root_node_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,coverage_cut,profile_oid}`. Nodes are canonically sorted persistent-tree objects; inherited/source roots, their selected ciphertext realizations, and epoch records are constructed first. The four exact AAD domains are:

```text
H("fgdb:key-envelope-child:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  graph, branch, envelope_epoch, parent_node_kind, child_range,
  child_oid, canonical(child_ciphertext_ref), wrap_profile, envelope_key_id)
H("fgdb:key-envelope-inherit:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  target_graph, target_branch, target_envelope_epoch,
  source_graph, source_branch, source_envelope_epoch, source_root_oid,
  canonical(source_root_ciphertext_ref),
  maximum_logical_command_seq, maximum_marker, wrap_profile, target_envelope_key_id)
H("fgdb:key-envelope-write:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  graph, branch, envelope_epoch, write_epoch_record_oid,
  allowed_creation_range, wrap_profile, envelope_key_id)
H("fgdb:branch-object-dek-wrap:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  logical_oid, ciphertext_id, dek_id, graph, branch, write_epoch,
  creation_logical_command_seq, wrap_profile, write_key_id)
```

The stored AAD bytes must equal the canonical transcript; a digest alone is not usable AAD. `KeyEnvelopeGrant` is built after its root and selected root ciphertext and binds `{grant_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,graph,branch,envelope_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,envelope_epoch,write_epoch?,coverage_cut,mode:SnapshotAtHead|AdvancingBranch,recipient_id,recipient_public_key_id,wrapped_root_object_dek,wrapped_envelope_key,wrap_profile,grant_aad,issuer,policy_epoch,revocation_index,issued_at,expiry?,signature}`. Its AAD is `canonical("fgdb:key-envelope-recipient:v1", every preceding scope/identity/coverage/mode/StrongCiphertextRef field except wrapped bytes/signature)`. A snapshot grant can name only a frozen closed root. An advancing grant intentionally covers new wraps under the named active epoch until rotation; a later epoch requires a new ordered grant. A live grant/edge pins its exact named ciphertext even if compaction creates another realization of the same logical root/node.

The entire physical/logical closure for a key-boundary transition is finalized **before** ordering. `BranchForkBundle` is `{expected_install_logical_command_seq,transition_nonce,parent,parent_expected_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,parent_expected_envelope_epoch,parent_expected_write_epoch,child_branch_id,child_policy,closed_parent_envelope_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,closed_parent_write_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,frozen_parent_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,frozen_parent_root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,parent_successor_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],parent_successor_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,parent_successor_manifest_ref:StrongRef<BranchManifest>,child_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],child_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,child_manifest_ref:StrongRef<BranchManifest>,grant_refs[StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeGrant>],complete_object_wrap_ciphertext_realization_inventory,closure_digest}`. `BranchGrantBundle` is `{expected_install_logical_command_seq,transition_nonce,operation:SnapshotAtHead|StartOrContinueAdvancing|RevokeAdvancing,branch,expected_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,expected_envelope_epoch,expected_write_epoch,closed_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],frozen_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>?,frozen_root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef?,successor_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],successor_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,successor_manifest_ref:StrongRef<BranchManifest>,grant_or_revocation_record_refs[StrongRef],complete_object_wrap_ciphertext_realization_inventory,closure_digest}`. The bundle is built bottom-up under a stable prepared owner: epoch records → ciphertexts/encodings/placements/openers → `StrongCiphertextRef` availability certificates → envelope nodes/roots → grants/manifests → bundle. Its payload-availability certificate covers that exact closed inventory and excludes only the future control command.

`BranchForkSpec` is `{bundle_ref:StrongRef<BranchForkBundle>,bundle_payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>,expected_parent_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,expected_parent_envelope_epoch,expected_parent_write_epoch,expected_install_logical_command_seq,transition_nonce,terminal_audit_gate}`. `BranchGrantSpec` is `{bundle_ref:StrongRef<BranchGrantBundle>,bundle_payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>,expected_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,expected_envelope_epoch,expected_write_epoch,expected_install_logical_command_seq,transition_nonce,terminal_audit_gate}`. Apply creates no key material, ciphertext, placement, envelope node, epoch record, grant, or manifest and performs no ambient physical selection: it byte-validates the complete bundle/certificate, exact expected head/epochs/sequence/nonce, closure disjointness and grant subset laws, then installs the already-known manifests/registries atomically. Snapshot issue and revocation bundles encode close→frozen root→double rotation; advancing issue may bind the exact active root/epoch without rotation. A stale head, epoch, sequence, certificate, or realization fails with no partial installation. Expiry without an ordered revocation/rotation does not claim cryptographic cutoff. Envelope reachability is part of GC/key-destruction/backup inventory. Fork/handoff/rotation tests attempt sibling, post-fork-parent, post-snapshot, post-revocation, expired-grant, stale-prepared-wrap, merge overbreadth, restore, crash at every bundle-build/order/apply boundary, and collected-key decryption and require fail-closed denial.

**MergeRecord / BranchMergeLedger.** A squash `MergeRecord` retains `{merge_token,merge_request_commitment,target,target_basis:StrongMarkerRef,source_heads[StrongMarkerRef],merge_bases[StrongMarkerRef],imported_range_tokens[{branch,first:WeakMarkerIdentity,last:WeakMarkerIdentity,base:WeakMarkerIdentity,chain_digest}],imported_range_keys[],resolution_policy_oid,resolution_digest,final_effect_digest}` and is linked from capsule/marker. Range tokens are weak provenance, not target ancestry or implicit retention. Pre-order `MergePrepareSpec` is `{client_request_nonce,request_commitment,candidate_merge_token,capability_generation,capability_nonce,capability_verifier_key_epoch,capability_expiry}`; the coordinator mints random token/nonce before ordering, and apply uses no entropy. `MergeOutcomeCapability` MACs `{format,issuer/key epoch,database_security_namespace_id,target,tenant/principal authority digest,merge_token,request_commitment,capability_generation,capability_nonce,policy/revocation,expiry}`. The ledger first maps `{tenant,principal,target,client_request_nonce}` to the chosen token plus these reproducible capability fields before evaluation; a same-request retry reconstructs them, a different proposed candidate is ignored after success, and conflicting commitment reuse is rejected. `ImportedRangeKey` hashes `{database namespace,target graph/branch,source branch/range/chain digest,merge semantics,resolution policy}` and excludes the mutable target basis. `BranchMergeLedgerRoot` contains `outcomes[merge_token -> {original_request,capability_fields,basis:WeakMarkerIdentity,InFlight|Committed{target_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity,final_effect_digest}|Rejected{stable_reason_digest}}]` plus `coverage_domains[H(namespace,target,source_branch,source_chain_domain,merge_semantics,resolution_policy) -> normalized_nonoverlapping_ranges[{first:WeakMarkerIdentity,last:WeakMarkerIdentity,chain_digest,imported_range_key}]]`. Transaction apply validates the prepared token/request/range-key set and installs the terminal outcome, normalized coverage, and merge marker atomically. Token retries return the original outcome; interval lookup detects exact and partial overlap, which rejects `AlreadyImported` or applies only a declared canonical uncovered remainder. Both maps are non-forgetting idempotency state preserved across checkpoint/history cuts, backup/restore, reconfiguration, and GC.

**PayloadReceipt / PayloadAvailabilityCertificate / ConfigPayloadFloor / GcEpoch.** `RemotePreparedIdentity { storage_member,prepared_ownership_id,base_closure_inventory_digest,latest_record_observation:NonRetainingRemoteObservation{record_digest:WeakDigest,observed_prepared_payload_root_generation} ? }` names the stable signed ownership promise; the optional diagnostic is neither a local ObjectId nor a reachability edge. A receipt binds `{database_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,configuration_state_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,payload_predicate_digest,storage_member,failure_domain,local_writer_fence_epoch,prepared_owner:RemotePreparedIdentity,encoding_and_placement_requirements[],symbol/source-block coverage,fsync_generation,proposal_valid_through?,nonce}` and a domain-separated member signature/MAC. The signer must still hold the matching `WriterLeaseGuard/FenceToken`; a receiver verifies the epoch against the member's current fenced identity/configuration before using the receipt. Successor records preserve that ownership/base closure and may only strengthen current closure. `proposal_valid_through` limits freshness for forming a new proposal; it is never a storage lease, retention horizon, or deletion permission. A certificate repeats namespace/incarnation, the exact configuration ref/predicate digest, canonically lists receipt refs, exact base logical-object plus encoding/placement requirements, FEC recoverability calculation, verifier version, and threshold signature.

Installed `ConfigPayloadFloor` is `{ basis:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,closed_through_raft_index,closed_through_logical_command_seq,current_config_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,prospective_joint_config_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>?,prospective_final_config_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,failure_domain_policy,current_checkpoint:WeakCheckpointIdentity,checkpoint_state_vector_digest:WeakDigest,command/marker_suffix_endpoints,typed_mandatory_inventory_root:StrongRef<MandatoryInventory>,prepared_root_generations_and_ownership_ids,per_domain_receipts_and_acks }`; its ObjectId is its floor identity. It has no strong edge to its basis root, checkpoint/vector, transition spec, or applied command. `MandatoryInventory` entries are tagged `RetainedStrong{class,ref}` or `CurrentCheckpointObservation{checkpoint:WeakCheckpointIdentity,checkpoint_state_vector_digest:WeakDigest,logical_inventory_digest,availability_receipt_refs[StrongRef]}`; the latter's logical identities and receipt requirements are comparison/availability evidence, never reachability edges. The inventory covers every payload/vector class, prepared/ordered command, delivered baseline/delta cursor and lease, replay/archive, all three external continuities, backups/legal holds, keys, and configuration state. Floor validation requires its checkpoint observation to equal the separately strong current `LogicalStatePayload.recovery_checkpoint_ref`; operational checkpoint replacement is valid only with §5.4's paired refreshed floor, whose checkpoint projection excludes the prior floor. Initial installation is the `CheckpointInstalled -> Operational` bootstrap command. Prefix/checkpoint drift requires candidate extension/recomputation before installation; retirement requires a final floor committed after and covering through `CommitNew`. `GcProposal` is the pre-order basis/acknowledgement/safe-point spec and uses weak basis identities. Applied `GcDecisionRecord { proposal_ref:StrongRef<GcProposal>,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef,stable_configuration,config_payload_floor_ref,retention_map_digest,typed_root_validation_digest,decision }` contains the result without being named by its input. Only a committed accepting decision may release committed or receipted obligations.

**KeyWrap / KeyDestroyRecord / BackupManifest.** `KeyWrap` binds `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,logical_oid,ciphertext_id,dek_id,scope:Recipient|Database|BranchEpoch{graph,branch,write_epoch,creation_logical_command_seq}|Replica|Backup,wrap_algorithm,wrap_key_id,wrap_key_epoch,wrapped_dek,aad_bytes,aad_digest,issuer_signature}`; for `BranchEpoch`, AAD must be exactly the branch-object transcript above, while every other scope has its own registered transcript. Namespace-key escrow uses a separately typed `ObjectIdKeyWrap` for `K_oid`. Rewrap creates only a new wrap; data re-encryption creates a new `CiphertextId` and its `EncodingId` realizations. `KeyDestroyProposal` binds the key, stable configuration, root-slot generations, checkpoint/configuration floors, generated scanned-root-class inventory (including branch epoch records, envelope nodes/roots/grants, and advancing-grant obligations), zero-reference proof, backup/legal-hold acknowledgements, and threshold authorization. Its applied command moves the key to `DestroyPending`. `KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec` binds that proposal, authenticated external destruction receipt, and an unchanged-or-stronger floor. The applied `KeyDestroyRecord` is `{proposal_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestroyProposal>,finalize_spec_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec>,applied_finalize_control_ref:AppliedControlRef,verified_floor_digest,destruction_receipt}`. No state reaches `Destroyed` if any reachable ciphertext, identity/envelope/write key, grant obligation, signing/verifier obligation, replay/DP/outcome/delivery/audit record, prepared owner, backup, or prospective configuration can still require the key.

`BackupState` is the closed posture union `Local{logical_state_root_ref,checkpoint/vector refs,current/prospective configuration/floor,prepared root/certificate/remote-trust and retention roots,retained stream floor}|Sharded{barrier_global_prefix,global_state_root/checkpoint/vector/meta configuration/floor/topology refs,global retained-stream/conflict/prepared/certificate/remote-trust and retention roots,sorted_shards[{shard_id,state_root_ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<ShardLogicalStateRoot>,checkpoint/vector/configuration/floor/history-inventory/active-projection/key/derived/prepared/certificate/remote-obligation evidence,operational_barrier_ref}],complete_group_and_partition_commitment,activation_or_restore_fence}`. Every shard is Operational and applied or proved irrelevant through exactly the barrier; each shard quorum signs its closure and Meta signs the aggregate. `BackupManifest` carries database/security namespace/incarnation, escrowed `K_oid`, latest identity/privacy/audit continuities and resolvers, identity mode, this `BackupState`, exact logical/commit/base/anti-rollback range, mandatory/policy object and prepared inventories, branch-key/grant/merge/DP/replay/cursor/delivery/audit evidence, distributed key/derived/remote grants, format matrix, signer thresholds, signatures, and transparency. Legacy Local manifests remain valid after activation and are never reinterpreted as Sharded. Unknown posture, group, inventory, trust, or barrier fields fail closed.

Same-identity restore never relabels an old-incarnation root. `RecoveryIncarnationProjection` is a generated exhaustive graph transform `{source_backup_manifest_ref,old_incarnation,new_incarnation,sorted_object_entries[ReencodeUnderNewIncarnation{old identity,new canonical body recipe,reference rewrite map}|ReuseIncarnationNeutral{identity,proof class}|Reject{reason}],root/field coverage digest,semantic-equivalence digest}`. Every incarnation-bearing canonical/control/security/config/Raft/prepared/certificate/key/audit/capability object and reference is re-encoded and rehashed under the new incarnation; only registered incarnation-neutral payloads are reusable. Old signatures/config evidence cannot authorize new objects. Missing/duplicate/unclassified objects fail closed.

`SameIdentityRecoveryBridgeSpec` is the one bootstrap exception `{restore_epoch,backup_manifest_ref,old-cluster external fence,RecoveryIncarnationProjection refs,new Local or Meta+Shard groups/configurations/checkpoints/floors,allocation epoch reservation,rotated signing/wrap/verifier keys,identity/privacy/audit continuity evidence,cursor/lease and distributed prepared-resolution plan,complete field/object coverage,terminal_audit_gate}`. Its new-incarnation `SameIdentityRecoveryBridgeRecord` has a typed nonretaining `PriorIncarnationBridge` predecessor and constructs the first `RecoveryReconciling` state/log without asking an ordinary new-incarnation command to validate as old. Local recovery orders every reconciliation successor, proves zero unresolved prepared/audit/cursor obligations, then `LocalRestoreActivationSpec` reaches Operational.

Sharded restore stages Meta and every shard under one `RestoreEpoch` in `RecoveryReconciling`, unreachable to clients. Each shard applies its projection, resolves/retains prepared decisions through the new Meta authority, and emits `RestoreShardReadyBarrier {SameGroupCertificateHeader,restore_epoch,global cut,state/checkpoint/config/floor/closure digests,zero-unresolved-or-explicitly-retained obligations}`. Meta orders `GlobalRestoreActivationSpec` over the complete barrier set and continuity/identity reconciliation; shards consume its certified activation and emit applied acks. Only `RestoreVisibilityCommit` with every ack allows endpoint advertisement and ordinary `Operational` work; partial barriers/retries remain fail-closed and idempotent. The old-cluster fence and backup lease remain held through visibility commit. Clone restore instead rebuilds namespace/ObjectIds/encryption and re-signs the entire Local or Sharded closure; it never imports old cross-group authority as current.

**ReplayManifest / executable and archive closure.** `ReplayCompleteness` is `Replayable|StructuralReplay|VerifiableIfArtifactsSupplied|AuditOnly` with explicit class lists. `ArchiveObjectIdentity` is nonlocal and never a local reachability edge. `ReplayObjectRef<T>` is exactly `LocalStrong{ref:StrongRef<T>}|CertifiedRemote{ref:CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<T>}|Archived{identity,expected_logical_object_id,expected_canonical_digest}`. CertifiedRemote requires a live matching authority configuration/trust selector/grant and participates in two-sided retention; Archived resolves only through the active registry and never marks local data. Every slot uses `ReplayEvidenceRef<T> = Present{object:ReplayObjectRef<T>}|Unavailable{class,expected identity/digest?,reason}|Redacted{class,commitment?,policy}`. `ReplayLogicalStateEvidence = Local{state:ReplayEvidenceRef<LogicalStateRoot>}|Sharded{global_state:ReplayEvidenceRef<GlobalStateRoot>,topology:ReplayEvidenceRef<TopologyState>,exact_global_prefix,sorted_shard_states[ReplayEvidenceRef<ShardLogicalStateRoot>],complete_partition_commitment}`; a Sharded grade is no stronger than its weakest required group/evidence lease.

`ReplayManifest` binds `{format major/minor,slot schema,database/security namespace/incarnation,logical/commit seq,logical_state:ReplayLogicalStateEvidence,graph bindings,topology/policy/revocation epochs,language/semantic/scalar/numeric profiles,answer requirement/result contract,logical/physical plan IDs,bound/normalized query,typed parameters,replay authority,module/UDF set,external inputs,derived generation snapshots,decision cards/policies/evidence,executable artifacts,structural projection,result encoding/digest,structural completeness,archive requirements,created HLC}`. The generated slot schema derives the maximum grade: Replayable requires every execution-semantic Local or Sharded slot live; structural replay requires its typed projection; supply-later carries all identities/digests; audit/redaction is explicit. Live effective grade may only weaken as any local, certified-remote, or archive trust/lease/authority fails. Legacy Local manifests survive activation unchanged.

`ExecutableArtifactSet` binds `{ exact_binary:ReplayObjectRef | reproducible_build_closure[ReplayObjectRef], source_tree:ReplayObjectRef?, rust_toolchain:ReplayObjectRef,target,cpu_feature_contract,runtime_allocator_config:ReplayObjectRef,vm_jit_compiler_artifacts[ReplayObjectRef],kernel_profile_registry:ReplayObjectRef,platform_abi:ReplayObjectRef,build_recipe:ReplayObjectRef,artifact_digest }`; exactly one executable route must be complete whenever this set is present. `StructuralReplayProjection` binds its reproduced event/data-shape classes, canonical projection schema, required evidence-slot classes, omitted/redacted classes, expected commitments, and output verifier. `ReplayArchiveRecord` is immutable `{ archive_id,generation,predecessor_record_digest:WeakDigest?,security_domain,resolver_profile_oid,authenticated_external_locator,archive_closure_digest:WeakDigest,sorted_object_inventory[{identity:ArchiveObjectIdentity,expected_logical_object_id,expected_canonical_digest,length}],availability_commitment,lease_not_before,lease_not_after,status:Active|Revoked|Expired,signer_set_epoch,signatures }`. Its inventory/closure explicitly excludes the record itself, `ReplayRegistry`, and the locally rooted manifest, so archive and manifest identities can be constructed in the order `external evidence inventory -> archive record -> manifest -> registry` without a digest cycle. `ReplayRegistry` maps `manifest_id -> {manifest:StrongRef<ReplayManifest>,lease/status}` and `archive_id -> latest_record:StrongRef<ReplayArchiveRecord>`. Renewal creates a logical-command-sequenced successor after re-verifying the entire inventory. Revocation/expiry never asserts deletion; consensus first removes the registry availability edge, after which ordinary GC may release otherwise-unrooted local manifest objects/records. A manifest is advertised `Replayable` only while every required local object opens and every archive requirement resolves through an active, unexpired, trusted record with a matching inventory/closure digest. Resolver credentials and replay contents require scoped `Replay` authority; capability-safe lookup does not disclose whether another authority's manifest/archive exists.

**Authorization, durable capabilities, DP, resources, and audit records.** `MutationPermitRecord` is `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,tenant,principal,issuer,authority_ceiling,authority_digest,policy_semantics_oid,policy_epoch,revocation_index,exact_role_bearing_read_bindings,role_free_write_coordinates,snapshot_scope,operation_scope,nonce,expiry,signer_epoch,signature_or_mac_transcript}`. `ReadPermitRecord` is the distinct no-write format `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,tenant,principal,issuer,authority_ceiling,authority_digest,policy_semantics_oid,policy_epoch,revocation_index,exact_role_bearing_read_bindings,allowed_snapshot_scope,allowed_query/operator/disclosure_scope,result_answer_contract_ceiling,nonce,expiry,signer_epoch,signature_or_mac_transcript}`; it has no write coordinate, mutation capability, or empty-effect convention. `AuthorizationLease` carries the same common scope plus its lease/revalidation fields. Rust exposes only verified nonconstructible wrappers.

`AuthorizationAuditGate` is exactly `StructurallyInapplicable{system_authority_class}|NotRequired{completeness_profile_oid,policy_decision_digest}|Required{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>}`. `AuthorizationDecisionRecord` is the closed tag `Mutation{permit_ref:StrongRef<MutationPermitRecord>,permit_scope_digest,tenant,principal,final_effect_digest,write_and_hidden_cascade_commitment,policy_epoch,revocation_index,decision,authorization_audit_gate}` | `Read{read_decision_ref:StrongRef<ReadAuthorizationDecisionRecord>}` | `Lifecycle{lifecycle_decision_ref:StrongRef<LifecycleAuthorizationDecisionRecord>}` | `GlobalMutation{global_decision_ref:StrongRef<GlobalAuthorizationDecisionRecord>}`. `ReadAuthorizationDecisionRecord` is `{registration_ref:StrongRef<GlobalAttemptRegistration>?,read_permit_ref:StrongRef<ReadPermitRecord>,permit_scope_digest,tenant,principal,exact_read_graph_bindings,read_routing_or_local_view_commitment,read_witness_commitment,authority_projection_digest,policy_epoch,revocation_index,result_answer_contract,disclosure_contract_digest,canonical_result_digest,decision,authorization_audit_gate:AuthorizationAuditGate}`. `LifecycleAuthorizationDecisionRecord` is the pre-result/no-effect form `{operation:RegisterAttempt|CancelActiveAttempt|PrepareAdmissionControl|StatusOrMaintenance,authority_permit_ref:AuthorityPermitRef?,tenant,principal,authority_ceiling_digest,sequence_neutral_spec_body_digest,requested_snapshot_or_scope_commitment,no_effect_or_control_effect_class,policy_epoch,revocation_index,decision,authorization_audit_gate:AuthorizationAuditGate}`. RegisterAttempt requires `Lifecycle` bound to its permit/spec before registration exists; PrepareAdmission requires `GlobalMutation` bound to the exact union-wide record; ReadClose requires `Read` whose registration/routing/witness/result fields byte-match its spec. A mutation decision or fabricated zero effect cannot substitute. The mutation/global forms can be built from final effects before the terminal event, while the read form is built after the buffered canonical result is known but before release.

`TerminalAuditGate` is exactly `StructurallyInapplicable{system_authority_class}|NotRequired{completeness_profile_oid,policy_decision_digest}|Required{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>}`. A required terminal gate is valid only when all three objects and the earlier authorization gate agree on namespace/domain/profile/principal/request, the resolution strongly owns that event, and the typed outcome matches the command/spec. Local `TxnOutcomePreparationRecord` is `{txn_token,expected_prior_state:Absent|Submitted{state_version,state_digest},proposed_terminal_kind,final_effect_digest,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>,resource_transition_refs[StrongRef],terminal_audit_gate}`. W12 exclusively uses the separate `GlobalTxnOutcomePreparationRecord` exact schema above; no object is reinterpreted or wrapped as the other kind. `DurableCapabilityVerifierKey {issuer_id,key_id,key_epoch,algorithm,public_or_protected_verifier_material,not_before,verify_through,format_versions[],rotation_predecessor?,status}` is Chronicle-sequenced and strongly retained until no live `ResumeCapability`, `TxnOutcomeCapability`, `MergeOutcomeCapability`, or `ReadYourWritesCapability` can require it. Each capability uses the exact versioned field set, domain-separates its kind/version, MACs every field, and names this key; rotations never reinterpret bytes.

`PrivacyContinuityRecord` is the external-and-mirrored `{ privacy_accounting_domain_id,privacy_epoch,cumulative_renyi_state_commitment,request_tombstone_root,predecessor_digest,external_registry_id,cas_version,status,issued_at,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures }`. `PrivacyLedgerState` canonically maps identity-level principals/aliases to composition state and debits, records the exact continuity head/receipt chain, and carries policy/mechanism epochs plus retention floor. `DpRequestKey` contains the stable privacy domain and request idempotency identity; cluster incarnation is provenance, not an accounting reset.

`DpRequestRecord` binds that canonical key, predecessor/state-transition digest, and exactly one state payload: `Prepared{no_sensitive_access,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef}`; `Abandoned{stable_reason,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef}`; `Charged{budget_debit,external_charge_receipt_ref:StrongRef,encrypted_seed_ref:StrongRef,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef}`; `Computing{same_charge_receipt_and_seed_refs,attempt_generation,no_output=true,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef}`; `ResultCommitted{same_charge_receipt_and_seed_refs,encrypted_result_ref:StrongRef,result_digest,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef}`; or `Delivered{budget_debit,external_charge_receipt_ref:StrongRef,encrypted_seed_ref:StrongRef,encrypted_result_ref:StrongRef,result_digest,delivery_receipt_digest,delivery_channel_class,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef}`. Each input is a sequence-neutral `DpTransitionSpec`; results cite the already known role-tagged command and sequence through `AppliedControlRef`. `DpRequestIndex` uniqueness-serializes the key and roots the latest record; seed/result/receipt refs and key wraps remain strong through the privacy/retry floor. Only `Prepared` can become `Abandoned`; no transition after external/local charge releases debit or exposes a data-dependent signal before `ResultCommitted`.

`AuditTicket` is `{database_security_namespace_id,audit_domain_id,cluster_incarnation_provenance,tenant,principal_scope,ticket_sequence,event_class,request_digest,completeness_profile_oid,issued_at,sequencer_epoch,signature}`. `AuditEventRecord` strongly names that ticket and binds the identical namespace/domain/profile/principal/request plus `{authorization_decision_digest,outcome:TransactionMutation{final_effect_digest,transaction_effect_basis_commitment}|ControlMutation{control_kind,spec_body_digest,expected_state_conditions_digest,semantic_transition_basis_commitment}|ReadResult{canonical_result_digest}|Denied{decision_digest}|Failed{stable_error_class,no_effect_proof_digest}|Abandoned{typed_reason,no_effect_proof_digest},event_attested_at,signer_epoch,signature}`. The transaction basis digest covers only pre-event sequence-neutral effect/coordinate/schema/constraint/resource/authorization/semantics/token inputs and excludes capsule/command/certificate identities, terminal gate, assigned sequence/HLC/marker/chain fields. The control body digest excludes `terminal_audit_gate`; its semantic-transition basis is the pre-order relation committed by that body and the expected conditions, never an applied result/root. `AuditTicketResolution` repeats ticket scope and is `{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,terminal:Completed{event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>}|Denied{event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>}|Failed{event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>}|Abandoned{event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>,typed_no_effect_reason},resolution_attested_at,signature}`; every terminal is therefore event-bound. The two `*_attested_at` fields are signed pre-order observations only; neither is the canonical apply-assigned `logical_command_hlc`. Apply verifies the full later command/result as the deterministic extension of the committed bases.

`AuditContinuityRecord` is the external-and-mirrored `{database_security_namespace_id,audit_domain_id,audit_epoch,highest_ticket_sequence,ticket_index_commitment,unresolved_ticket_commitment,audit_chain_head_digest,predecessor_digest,external_registry_id,cas_version,status:Complete{profile_oid}|PermanentGap{latest_transition_ref:StrongRef<AuditCompletenessTransitionRecord>,current_profile_oid},last_transition:TicketIssued{ticket_digest}|TicketResolved{ticket_digest,resolution_digest,event_digest,candidate_root_digest:WeakDigest}|CompletenessChanged{transition_ref:StrongRef<AuditCompletenessTransitionRecord>},signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}`. The registry retains authenticated ticket/event/resolution/transition bytes or authenticated resolver refs. `AuditExternalCasReceipt` is built **after** the returned continuity record and binds `{external_registry_id,prior_head_digest,returned_head_digest,prior_cas_version,returned_cas_version,transition_kind,subject_digest,registry_signature_set}`; the continuity record never points forward to its receipt.

Exact `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec` is `{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,expected_prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,expected_prior_cas_version,returned_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,external_cas_receipt_ref:StrongRef<AuditExternalCasReceipt>}`. Its validator requires the direct `TicketIssued` successor, exact sequence increment, exact addition to ticket/unresolved commitments, matching receipt subject and CAS versions, and no unrelated field change; recovery of an externally issued but not-yet-mirrored ticket runs this same idempotent validator. The fence is the role tag `AuditVisibilityFenceRef = Local{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,candidate:AuditCandidateRef::Local,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>} | Meta{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,candidate:AuditCandidateRef::Meta,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>}`; shard groups never originate a global semantic audit fence. Exact `AuditTerminalSpec` is `{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,expected_pending_ticket_digest:WeakDigest,event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>}`; it is the non-mutating/pre-effect terminal path and apply rejects any ticket/event/resolution scope or outcome mismatch. Transaction preparation and every state-changing control command carry the same exact triple through `TerminalAuditGate::Required`.
