Exact `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec` is `{active_fence_digest:WeakDigest,ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,candidate:AuditCandidateRef,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>,expected_prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,expected_prior_cas_version,returned_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,external_cas_receipt_ref:StrongRef<AuditExternalCasReceipt>}`. Its validator requires the candidate role/group/blocked sequence/root to byte-match the active fence and the mirror command's `AppliedControlRef`, then enforces the complete equality/direct-successor relation in §12.8 before removing exactly that fence. `AuditCompletenessTransitionRecord` is created before its external CAS and is `{audit_domain_id,prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,exact_missing_ticket_or_event_interval,missing_commitment,evidence_or_reason,old_profile_oid,new_profile_oid,permanent_effective_audit_epoch,authorization,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}`. Exact `AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec` is `{transition_ref:StrongRef<AuditCompletenessTransitionRecord>,expected_prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,expected_prior_cas_version,returned_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,external_cas_receipt_ref:StrongRef<AuditExternalCasReceipt>}`; it validates the returned record as the direct `CompletenessChanged` successor for that transition and validates the receipt against both heads and CAS versions. Only that ordered transition may resume at the permanently weakened profile. Ticket admission, mirror, recovery, and completeness transition use `TerminalAuditGate::StructurallyInapplicable` under system-audit authority; terminal consumes the existing ticket.

`AuditCloneBoundary` is `{source_database_security_namespace_id,source_audit_domain_id,source_continuity_head_digest,target_database_security_namespace_id,target_audit_domain_id,clone_manifest_ref,retained_source_evidence_contract,source_signatures,target_signatures}` and never rewrites source tickets into the target domain. `AuditSegment` is a contiguous signed range with previous-chain digest, ticket/resolution ranges, event records, redaction profile, signing epoch, and external-anchor ref. `AuditTicketIndex` makes every issued ticket pending or uniquely resolved and retains its event, external receipt, and mirror status across recovery. `AuditCheckpoint` commits retained ticket/event floors and heads, unresolved-ticket set, continuity/gap heads, signer-rotation chain, and anchor. Missing external evidence disables completeness-gated operations; it never silently weakens the advertised profile.

**WitnessPolicy / TransparencyCheckpoint.** `WitnessPolicy` is `{format_version,log_id,security_domain_id,policy_epoch,claim_class:EquivocationDetection|NonEquivocation,ordered_witnesses[{witness_id,key_id,verification_key,endpoint_identity,optional_cross_log_authority}],n,threshold_t,byzantine_bound_f,signature_profile,consistency_proof_profile,durable_head_state_profile,anti_rollback_profile,authenticated_gossip_profile:None|Required{transport_auth_profile,peer_identity_registry,checkpoint_message_schema,replay_window,evidence_retention_floor,maximum_convergence_delay},activation_log_size,maximum_checkpoint_age,cross_log_policy:None|Required{ordered_authorities,threshold},rotation:Genesis|JointSuccessor{predecessor_policy_ref:StrongRef<WitnessPolicy>}}`. Canonical validation requires exactly `n` unique ordered witnesses, `0 <= f < t <= n`, supported signature/consistency/persistence profiles, and—before `claim_class=NonEquivocation` is usable—`2t > n + f`. A detection claim that relies on gossip requires the complete authenticated profile; an unnamed/best-effort channel proves nothing. Each honest witness durably stores `{log_id,security_domain_id,policy_oid,last_size,last_root,anti_rollback_counter}` before acknowledging a signature; it signs only a verified append-only consistency extension, never two roots at one size or non-extending histories. Rollback or loss of this state disables that witness until an authenticated recovery/rotation procedure; it cannot silently start fresh.

`TransparencyCrossLogReceipt` is `{authority_id,authority_key_id,source_log_id,source_security_domain_id,source_policy_ref:StrongRef<WitnessPolicy>,source_log_size,source_root,target_log_id,target_log_size,target_inclusion_commitment,target_inclusion_proof,observed_at,not_after,signature}`. `TransparencyCheckpoint` is `{format_version,mode:LocalRollbackDetection|WitnessedEquivocationDetection{witness_policy_ref:StrongRef<WitnessPolicy>}|WitnessedNonEquivocation{witness_policy_ref:StrongRef<WitnessPolicy>},log_size,global_mmr_root,branch_head_commitment_root,security_domain_commitment,previous_checkpoint_digest:WeakDigest,consistency_proof_from_previous,issued_at,operator_key_id,operator_signature,sorted_witness_signatures[{witness_id,key_id,signature}],cross_log_receipt_refs[StrongRef<TransparencyCrossLogReceipt>],rotation_proof:None|JointActivation{old_policy_ref:StrongRef<WitnessPolicy>,new_policy_ref:StrongRef<WitnessPolicy>,old_sorted_signatures[],new_sorted_signatures[]}}`. Every signature covers the domain-separated canonical checkpoint body excluding all signature arrays. A witnessed mode requires its policy identity, freshness, threshold of distinct configured keys, and any required cross-log receipts.

Canonical cross-log validation requires `1 <= cross_log_policy.threshold <= count(unique ordered authorities)`; at least that many receipts come from distinct configured authority/key pairs, and every accepted receipt's source policy/log/security domain/size/root equals the current checkpoint's policy/log/domain/`log_size`/global root commitment exactly. Its target inclusion proof must verify under the named target log/size, `observed_at <= issued_at <= not_after`, and age must satisfy both policies; duplicates, foreign source roots, stale inclusions, or self-asserted target sizes fail. `JointActivation` additionally requires: the old policy equals the currently active policy; `new.rotation == JointSuccessor{predecessor=old}`; old/new log and security-domain identities are equal; `new.policy_epoch > old.policy_epoch`; checkpoint mode names the new policy; `log_size >= new.activation_log_size`; and the checkpoint body has valid distinct-key thresholds under both old and new policies. Only after that exact activation checkpoint may successors use the new policy alone.

The branch commitment is domain-separated and reveals no plain branch identity/head; authorized clients receive scoped inclusion/consistency proofs under the metadata-declassification policy, and mutually hidden branch sets use distinct security-domain logs. `LocalRollbackDetection` proves only consistency relative to a client's cached head. `WitnessedEquivocationDetection` promises durable evidence once conflicting heads reach the declared gossip/cross-log path. Only `WitnessedNonEquivocation` with a valid intersection-safe policy, honest durable-head assumption, consistency proofs, joint rotation, and freshness may claim split-view prevention. If any premise fails, verification fails closed or downgrades the advertised claim to detection/local scope; later gossip is never relabeled as prevention. **PolicyEpoch** is `{ policy_id,version,scope,logical_effect_class,pinned_table_oid,fallback_oid,evidence_refs[],previous_epoch_oid }`; statistical evidence may justify promotion but is never encoded as an invariant.

## Appendix B — Graph Intent Log (the semantic vocabulary)

Intents are deterministic commands captured at statement execution; they are **not** committed effects or Ripple deltas. Every intent has `{ intent_ordinal, intent_semantics_oid, graph_reference_bindings[], write_coordinate_bindings[], policy_epoch, captured_reads, structural_effect_class }`, while the enclosing proposal repeats the same `IntentSemanticsOid` and supplies its nonconstructible authorization permit and reservations. A mixed-semantics proposal is invalid. Temporary references/IDs are proposal-local and must be resolved through canonical allocator state before finalization.

```
CreateVertex   { tmp_ref, label_set, props }
DeleteVertex   { vid, cascade_policy }
AddLabel/RemoveLabel { vid, label }
AddEdge        { src, etype, dst, requested_key?, props }
RemoveEdge     { eid }
SetProp        { elem, name, value, merge_policy_id }
RemoveProp     { elem, name }
EnsureEdge     { src, etype, dst, constraint_id, props }
CompareAndSet  { elem, name, expected, value, mismatch: NoOp|StatementError|TxnAbort }
SetInsert      { elem, name, element, set_epoch }
SetRemove      { elem, name, element, observed_tags_or_remove_policy }
SetValidTime   { elem, from?, to? }
AssertSameAs   { a, b, confidence, source }
BulkLoad       { staged_run_oids, source_digest, logical_row_digest }
SchemaOp       { canonical_schema_operation }
```

LWW policies use canonical `EffectOrder { commit_seq, intent_ordinal, merge_ordinal, effect_ordinal }`, never element birth or an ambient wall clock. Set/counter/escrow/sketch modes name their exact algebra, tag/rights ledger, overflow behavior, and schema constraints. `ConsistencyClass` is derived only after composing the intent semantics with captured reads, active constraints, authority, and branch policy. Commutativity tables are caches of proved contextual results.

Finalization evaluates all commands and emits only canonical effects:

```text
CreateVertexEffect { permanent_vid, birth_ordinal, labels, canonical_props }
DeleteVertexEffect { vid, retirement_basis, retired_incident_eids[] }
LabelMembershipEffect { vid, label, before, after }
CreateEdgeEffect { permanent_eid, birth_ordinal, src, type, dst, canonical_key?, props }
DeleteEdgeEffect { eid, retirement_basis }
PropertyEffect { elem, property, before, after }
SchemaEffect { apply_basis, before_schema_oid, before_epoch,
               after_schema_oid, after_epoch }
ConstraintStateEffect { apply_basis, before_schema_root, before_schema_epoch,
                        after_schema_root, after_schema_epoch,
                        before_constraint_root, after_constraint_root }
ResourceChargeEffect { reservation_id, scope, before_charge, after_charge, reason }
```

Every coordinate-scoped effect is stored in `EffectEnvelope { graph, branch, effect_ordinal, effect }`; the envelope is the sole coordinate source, so nested effects cannot disagree with it. Database-global resource/audit effects use a separately tagged global envelope. `CommittedEffectSet` is sorted canonically, carries explicit before/after semantics, permanent IDs/BirthOrdinals, branch-aware retirement bases, constraint/authorization/resource evidence, and no conditional operation. The sequence-neutral, graph/branch/relation/schema/intent-semantics-keyed `LogicalDeltaTemplate` is derived from it and differential-tested against applying the intents once under the pinned `IntentSemanticsOid` to the recorded basis; only the committed `MarkerRef` turns it into an ordered `LogicalDeltaBatch`.

## Appendix C — GLA Operator Inventory (executor contracts)

Every physical implementation registers input/output factorization, strict/relaxed determinism, minimum resident set and spill algorithm, maximum work between cancellation checkpoints, incremental derivative or `none`, witness domain, authorization boundary, path preservation, input/output `AnswerContract` transfer or rejection, and legal `ReplanClass`. “Propagate” below means retain the complete upstream approximation provenance and apply a registered sound transformation; it never means relabel approximate data as exact. The initial normative matrix is:

| Family | Memory / spill | Incremental contract | Replan / witness contract | Answer-contract rule |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `ScanVertices/ScanEdges/Values` | bounded cursor; external batch buffers | linear derivative | partition boundary; label/type/range/gap witness | exact base cursor/value input emits `Exact` |
| `IndexProbe{btree,hash,fts,vector,path}` | bounded cursor plus candidate heap; exact tail path may spill | registered per index | before output unless continuation proved; generation/range/gap/watermark witness | emit the pinned generation contract; `Exact` requires exact index+tail completion |
| `HybridSearch` | spillable per-source candidate runs, fusion heap, rerank and expansion frontier | registered only for a complete fusion/expansion derivative; otherwise recompute | before output or a fully materialized candidate/fusion boundary; all source-generation, tail, candidate, fusion, authorization, and expansion witnesses | compose every source/stage; `Exact` only through complete exact sources or pinned exact fallback, otherwise emit fully qualified `Approximate` |
| `Expand/VarLengthExpand` | bounded descriptor cursor; factorized/path history spill | bounded-hop derivative only where registered | descriptor or checkpointed path frontier; adjacency ranges and path cuts | exact adjacency preserves `Exact`; approximate seed/input coverage propagates under a registered law |
| `PathFind` | spillable frontier, history sets, path DAG | registered mode/selector subsets only | no switch after emission without state transfer; full mode-aware witness | `Exact` requires exact graph/input and complete algorithm; approximation needs a selector-specific bound/recall law |
| `FreeJoin/HashJoin` | radix/grace partitions; partitioned COLT | bilinear/custom derivative | build/materialization barrier or verified state transfer; all input predicate witnesses | all-exact inputs yield `Exact`; any approximate input requires a registered join error/completeness transform |
| `LeftOuter/Semi/Anti/Apply/NullExtend` | spillable correlation/match state | custom or recompute | materialization boundary; absence and correlated-domain witnesses mandatory | absence-sensitive forms require exact negative domains for `Exact`; otherwise a registered approximation law or rejection |
| `Select/Project/Unnest/Flatten` | vector-bounded; flatten spillable | linear where expression is registered | batch boundary; preserve or explicitly transform factorization/path/witness laws | deterministic total transforms preserve `Exact`; approximate provenance is transformed, never erased |
| `Aggregate/Distinct` | radix-partitioned retained state | registered algebra with deletion law | completed partition or state transfer; group-domain and multiplicity witness | `Exact` only from exact complete inputs; approximation requires a registered estimator/error algebra |
| `OrderBy/Limit{offset,count}` | top-k heap or external stable merge sort | top-k custom; full sort normally recompute | no switch after emitted prefix; order/tie and early-stop gap witnesses | exact ordered prefix requires exact gap/completeness proof; approximate top-k carries recall/error and population |
| `SetOp{Union,Intersect,Except}` | partition-spillable multiplicity state | registered per ALL/DISTINCT form | materialization boundary; negative/right-side domains where applicable | all-exact inputs yield `Exact`; approximate difference/intersection requires a sound registered law |
| `Fixpoint` | LSM-backed arrangements and iteration spill | validated SCC only | iteration barrier; termination and recursive-domain witness | `Exact` requires exact seed/relations and convergence; approximate recursion is unavailable unless separately registered |
| `TemporalSlice/TemporalJoin` | interval-partition spill | registered interval algebra | interval boundary; system/valid-time ranges and gaps | preserves `Exact` only with complete temporal coverage; otherwise propagates qualified interval approximation |
| `SemiringMxV` | sparse/dense frontier spill | registered annotation algebra | iteration/frontier barrier; projection/capability/path semantics pinned | exact algebra+inputs yield `Exact`; numeric/coverage approximation requires its registered bound |
| `ProcedureCall` | declared per procedure; otherwise reject | none unless explicitly registered | none by default; authorized view only; external nondeterminism badge as required | signature independently declares answer-contract transfer and replay-input capture; external/nondeterministic execution may still be semantically exact but downgrades replay completeness, while an approximate procedure remains approximate even if perfectly replayable |
| `GraphConstruct` | spillable canonical key/value and path/provenance runs; generation-local dense ordinals allowed | registered pure construction derivative with deletion/multiplicity law | batch/materialization boundary; complete source/provenance witnesses and canonical `ViewElementRef` identity | pure deterministic construction preserves/propagates its inputs; it has no proposal or commit side effect |
| `Mutate` | proposal-local buffered intents/effects | emits canonical logical delta only after successful commit | never replanned after side-effect ordering; complete read/write/constraint/authorization witness | consumes `Exact` only; approximate data cannot authorize a mutation target/effect |
| `ViewDelta/CertEmit` | bounded envelope plus spillable forensic detail | stream tap | no semantic replan; watermark/evidence closure must remain exact | preserves and serializes the full input/output contract without upgrading it |

Any operator without a complete row, a total answer-contract rule, and conformance tests is unavailable, not implicitly “bounded.” Strict flatten/factorization, spill/no-spill, compaction, and legal replan variants are metamorphically required to produce identical canonical results **within the same answer contract and pinned approximate generation closure**. A transition that changes approximate candidates/topology is a new semantic generation, not an equivalent physical variant.

## Appendix D — FGP Protocol Contract

Connection states are only `TransportEstablished -> VersionNegotiated -> Authenticated -> Ready -> Draining -> Closed`. `Ready` owns at most one transaction child `Idle -> Begun -> CommitSubmitted -> Committed|Aborted|Unknown -> Idle`, zero or more query children `Accepted -> Bound -> Executing -> StreamingResults -> Completed|Cancelled|Failed`, and zero or more subscription/export children `Opening -> Baseline -> Delta -> Resetting|Ended`. The negotiated `concurrency_profile` declares permitted coexistence; baseline profiles serialize transaction-bound statements while allowing only explicitly independent autocommit children. `Draining` creates no child and closes only after each existing child has a terminal record. Every frame has `{ frame_len, protocol_version, frame_type, flags, request_id, stream_id }` and is rejected before allocation when it exceeds negotiated `FrameLimits`. Ephemeral statement/stream/query/active-transaction/reservation handles bind the current session; only the explicitly typed `ResumeCapability`, `MergeOutcomeCapability`, `ReadYourWritesCapability`, and `TxnOutcomeCapability` cross sessions, under §5.6/§9.5/§13/§14.3's namespace/incarnation, same-or-narrower-authority, expiry, revocation, rotation, replay, retention-floor, and capability-safe-lookup rules. A `ReplayManifest` ObjectId may be presented in a later authenticated session but conveys no authority; `REPLAY_*` always reauthorizes the complete closure. No generic “cursor,” “merge token,” “causal token,” or “transaction token” is implicitly transferable.

Normative frame families:

```text
HELLO{versions,features,client_nonce,limits,concurrency_profiles}
HELLO_ACK{version,features,server_nonce,limits,concurrency_profile,transcript_binding}
AUTH{token,channel_binding} / AUTH_REFRESH{token}
BEGIN{isolation,write_coordinates,default_snapshot_selector,read_your_writes_capability?} / BEGUN{txn_handle,txn_outcome_capability,snapshot_contract} / ROLLBACK{txn_handle}
PREPARE{text,language_contract_oid} / PREPARED{stmt_id,param_schema,prepared_template_digest,compatibility_contracts}
EXECUTE{stmt_id,params,consistency,read_your_writes_capability?,determinism,answer_requirement,fetch,resource_request}
EXECUTE_TEXT{text,language_contract_oid,params,consistency,read_your_writes_capability?,determinism,answer_requirement,fetch,resource_request}
RESULT_SCHEMA{schema,result_answer_contract} / RESULT_FRAME{flat|factorized,canonical_encoding_version}
RESULT_END{status,effective_snapshot,canonical_digest,read_your_writes_capability?,replay_manifest_ref?{oid,format_major,format_minor,completeness}}
COMMIT{txn_handle} / COMMIT_OUTCOME{txn_outcome_capability,committed(marker_ref,read_your_writes_capability)|aborted(reason)|unknown}
COMMIT_STATUS{txn_outcome_capability}
QUERY_CANCEL{request_id} / COMMIT_CANCEL{txn_handle}
CANCEL_EXPLANATION{lineage,exact_drain_state,statistical_estimate?}
SUBSCRIBE_BEGIN{definition,snapshot_mode,authority_mode}
SUBSCRIBE_READY{derived_identity_digest,graph_reference_bindings,delivery_frontier:Local|Global,resume_capability,baseline_lease_id,baseline_id,baseline_digest}
SNAPSHOT_BEGIN{baseline_lease_id,baseline_id,cursor_state_version,delivery_frontier:Local|Global,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,total_chunks,total_len,digest}
SNAPSHOT_CHUNK{baseline_lease_id,baseline_id,digest,chunk_ordinal,chunk_count,canonical_offset,payload} / SNAPSHOT_END{baseline_lease_id,baseline_id,digest}
SNAPSHOT_ACK{baseline_lease_id,baseline_id,baseline_digest,baseline_frontier:Local|Global,cursor_state_version,capability_generation}
SNAPSHOT_ACKED{rotated_resume_capability,cursor_state_version,acknowledged_frontier:Local|Global}
DELTA_BEGIN{delivery_lease_id,delivery_id,delivery_digest,
            envelope_header{format,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,
                            tenant_principal_authority_digest,derived_identity_digest,
                            baseline_id,start_frontier:Local|Global,resulting_frontier:Local|Global},
            output{delivered_payload_oid,output_schema,result_answer_contract,
                   canonical_encoding_version,canonical_payload_len,output_payload_digest},
            provenance:Atomic{source:CommittedDeltaSourceRef,source_batch_digest}|
                       Coalesced{source_role:Local|Global,first_batch_id,last_batch_id,
                                 ordered_source_commitment,source_count},total_chunks}
DELTA_CHUNK{delivery_id,delivery_digest,output_payload_digest,chunk_index,chunk_count,
            canonical_offset,payload}
DELTA_END{delivery_id,delivery_digest,output_payload_digest,proof_scope,proof?}
DATA_FRAGMENT{envelope_id,chunk_ordinal,row_ordinal,fragment_ordinal,total_fragments,
              canonical_row_len,row_digest,payload}
AUTHORITY_RESET{old_digest,new_digest,effective_frontier:Local|Global,new_baseline_id,posture_transition?}
ACK{delivery_lease_id,delivery_id,delivery_digest,resulting_frontier:Local|Global,
    cursor_state_version,capability_generation}
ACKED{rotated_resume_capability,cursor_state_version,resulting_frontier:Local|Global}
RESUME{resume_capability} / RESUMED{rotated_resume_capability,outstanding:Baseline{baseline_lease_id,baseline_id,baseline_digest,baseline_frontier:Local|Global}|Delta{delivery_lease_id,delivery_id,delivery_digest,resulting_frontier:Local|Global}|None,next_frontier:Local|Global?}
GAP{expected_frontier:Local|Global,available_from:Local|Global,new_baseline_contract}
PROOF{membership|range|consistency|checkpoint,scope}
REPLAY_GET{manifest_oid} / REPLAY_MANIFEST_BEGIN{manifest_oid,format_major,format_minor,completeness,total_chunks,total_len,digest}
REPLAY_MANIFEST_CHUNK{manifest_oid,chunk_ordinal,payload} / REPLAY_MANIFEST_END{manifest_oid,digest}
REPLAY_EXECUTE{manifest_oid,fetch,resource_request} / REPLAY_STATUS{manifest_oid,effective_completeness,archive_expiries[],missing_classes[]}
AUDIT_RECEIPT_REQUEST{request_id} / AUDIT_RECEIPT{ticket_ref,resolution_ref?,checkpoint_ref?}
FLOW_CREDIT{stream_id,bytes,rows} / STREAM_END
FEC_BEGIN{authenticated_ciphertext_record,authenticated_encoding_descriptor,placement_context,reservation}
FEC_SYMBOL{canonical_symbol_record_bytes}
ERROR{scope,code,retry_class,redacted_detail?} / GOODBYE
```

Frame-order validity does not replace value, authorization, decompression, or resource validation. `DELTA_BEGIN` carries every canonical envelope field needed to recompute `DeliveryDigest`, including the public delivered-output digest and complete atomic/coalesced provenance. The keyed payload/ObjectIds are opaque handles for clients without `K_oid`; they never substitute for validating the reassembled public logical-output digest. Every `DELTA_CHUNK` repeats delivery/output digests, index/count, and canonical offset, and its bytes occupy exactly that range in the stream hashed by `output_payload_digest`. A delta delivery, baseline snapshot, or replay manifest may exceed `FrameLimits`, so deterministic chunking prefers canonical row/record boundaries and every chunk is covered by the whole-envelope/payload digest. A legal canonical row larger than one frame is split only by `DATA_FRAGMENT` at deterministic byte offsets; the receiver validates declared total row length against its negotiated logical-row limit, reserves bounded assembly/spill resources before accepting bytes, verifies per-row and whole-envelope digests, and exposes nothing until the row and enclosing `*_END` are complete. Thus `max_frame_bytes` need not equal `max_logical_row_bytes`, and fragmentation never changes logical encoding. Clients apply/ACK only after matching `*_END`; an incomplete unacked delta is discarded and replayed with the same `DeliveryId`/digests on resume, never skipped via a frontier. An incomplete baseline is likewise discarded and replayed from offset zero under the same baseline lease/ID/digest; `SNAPSHOT_ACK` atomically transitions the durable cursor to `Active`, and no delta frame may precede `SNAPSHOT_ACKED`. A duplicate baseline/delta ACK or resume after a lost response returns the same pre-minted successor capability and state version. The tagged provenance makes atomic and coalesced delta ACK/resume semantics identical without pretending a coalesced range is one `LogicalDeltaBatch`. Cursor-state version/generation make all ACK transitions reproducible. `ReadYourWritesCapability` is issued only in a committed result/outcome and may be presented only in the explicit `BEGIN`/`EXECUTE*` fields; its validation may wait/route to the named visible prefix but cannot replace current query authorization. `replay_manifest_ref` is fixed-size metadata, not inline unbounded evidence; replay retrieval/execution requires current scoped authority and reports the effective grade after live closure/archive verification. Each `FEC_SYMBOL` payload is the exact canonical `SymbolRecord` from Appendix A, including all authenticated header fields and MAC; a receiver verifies it against the authenticated complete descriptor before admission. Compression/FEC is negotiated per stream after authenticated metadata and budget reservation. Result framing never changes canonical logical identity. HTTP/gRPC/WebSocket/Bolt adapters preserve transaction/idempotency semantics and define origin/CSRF, admin-listener, metrics authorization, header/trace-baggage, and decompression limits. All adapters, token parsing, bytecode validation, and nested/compressed/FEC envelopes have fuzz/conformance corpora.

## Appendix E — Working Bibliography (anchors reviewed for this plan)

Storage: Sortledton (PVLDB 15(6), 2022) · Teseo (PVLDB 14(6), 2021) · LiveGraph (PVLDB 13(7), 2020) · Aspen (PLDI 2019) · GraphOne (FAST 2019) · GTX / Spruce / RapidStore (2024–25) · RadixGraph (2026) · "Revisiting In-Memory Dynamic Graph Storage" (2025) · Dostoevsky/Fluid LSM (Dayan & Idreos, SIGMOD 2018) · S3-FIFO (Yang et al., SOSP 2023) · SuRF (Zhang et al., SIGMOD 2018). Processing: Kùzu (CIDR 2023) + "Columnar Storage and List-based Processing" (PVLDB 14(11)) + A+ Indexes · NPRR/AGM & Leapfrog Triejoin · EmptyHeaded (SIGMOD 2016) · Free Join (SIGMOD 2023) · ADOPT (2023) · HoneyComb (2025) · Umbra (CIDR 2020) · LeanStore · morsel-driven parallelism (SIGMOD 2014) · SPJM converged optimization (2024). Incremental: DBSP (PVLDB 16 / VLDBJ 2025, Lean-formalized; Feldera) · Differential/Timely Dataflow · streaming-graph SGQ work. Temporal: AeonG (PVLDB 17(6), 2024; VLDBJ 2025) · SQL:2011 system time · T-GQL, Clock-G. Languages: ISO/IEC 39075:2024 (GQL) · ISO/IEC 9075-16:2023 (SQL/PGQ) · GQL/PGQ pattern-matching & expressive-power papers · path-multiset representations (Martens et al.) · openCypher TCK. Vector: HNSW (Malkov & Yashunin) · DiskANN/Vamana · 2025–26 fresh-ANN and disaggregated-HNSW literature. Verification: FoundationDB simulation testing · Elle (Kingsbury & Alvaro) · Cahill/Fekete SSI · Serial Safety Net (Wang et al.) · asupersync formal-semantics & proof-lane artifacts. Distributed alternatives (evaluated, not adopted — §3.4, §14): Weaver refinable timestamps · G-Tran RDMA MV-OCC. Calibration & sequential statistics (§15.0): conformal prediction (Vovk, Gammerman & Shafer) and conformal risk control · game-theoretic probability, e-processes & anytime-valid inference (Shafer & Vovk; Ramdas, Grünwald, Vovk & Shafer; Ville 1939) · Wald's SPRT (1945) · Shiryaev–Roberts change detection · Bayesian online changepoint detection (Adams & MacKay 2007) · empirical Bayes / James–Stein (Robbins; Efron & Morris) · Good–Turing (1953) · robust estimation (Huber; Catoni 2012) · off-policy evaluation (Dudík, Langford & Li 2011) · learning-augmented algorithms (Lykouris & Vassilvitskii 2018). Control & operations (§16.6): CVaR (Rockafellar & Uryasev 2000) · extreme value theory / POT-GPD (Pickands 1975) · network calculus (Le Boudec & Thiran 2001) · max-plus algebra (Baccelli et al.) · Kingman's bound; Little's law · submodular maximization (Nemhauser, Wolsey & Fisher 1978; Krause & Golovin) · critical slowing down / early-warning signals (Scheffer et al. 2009). Consistency & distribution (§7.4, §14): CALM (Hellerstein & Alvaro, CACM 2020) · Red–Blue consistency (Li et al., OSDI 2012) · escrow transactions (O'Neil 1986) · SWIM (Das, Gupta & Motivala 2002) + Lifeguard (Dadgar et al. 2018) · closed timestamps (CockroachDB) · hybrid logical clocks (Kulkarni et al. 2014) · Merkle anti-entropy (DeCandia et al., Dynamo 2007) · consistent hashing with bounded loads (Mirrokni et al. 2016) · optimal transport (Villani; Cuturi's Sinkhorn 2013). Verifiability (§5.8): Certificate Transparency (Laurie; RFC 6962) · Merkle Mountain Ranges (Todd/opentimestamps lineage) · authenticated data structures (Merkle; Miller et al.) · PDP (Ateniese et al. 2007) / PoR (Juels & Kaliski 2007) · MTTDL Markov reliability models (Patterson et al. RAID lineage) · misuse-resistant AEAD/SIV (Rogaway & Shrimpton 2006) · differential privacy (Dwork et al. 2006; Rényi accounting, Mironov 2017; smooth sensitivity, Nissim, Raskhodnikova & Smith 2007). Verification methodology (§15): lineage-driven fault injection (Alvaro, Rosen & Hellerstein, SIGMOD 2015) · delta debugging (Zeller & Hildebrandt 2002) · record/replay of nondeterminism boundaries (rr; Mozilla) · provenance semirings (Green, Karvounarakis & Tannen, PODS 2007) · persistent union-find (Conchon & Filliâtre 2007) and offline dynamic connectivity (segment-tree-over-time folklore). Executor engineering (§8.7): AMAC (Kocberber, Falsafi & Grot, PVLDB 2015) · radix hash joins (Balkesen et al., ICDE 2013) · tail at scale hedging (Dean & Barroso, CACM 2013). Benchmarks: LDBC SNB / Graphalytics / FinBench. Market context (2026): GQL adoption in Spanner Graph & Fabric; Kùzu wind-down and forks; GraphRAG/agent-memory adoption analyses and their governance/freshness gap findings.

## Appendix F — Invariant and Evidence Registries

This twenty-row table is the normative invariant spine during design. G0 materializes it as checked-in `invariants.toml` with owner, checker paths, dependencies, claim scope, and gate; no Genesis implementation starts before that file exists. CI then rejects a missing checker. Statistical, configuration-model, and empirical gates live in separate registries below and may never masquerade as these invariants.

| ID | Invariant | Enforcement |
|---|---|---|
| FG-INV-01 | Within one database security namespace/incarnation and scoped outcome-capability domain, a durable `txn_token` maps to at most one terminal outcome and final-effect digest; submit, commit, and typed `TxnAbortSpec` compare-and-transition accept only `Absent` or the exact recorded `Submitted` version, a matching terminal retry is a no-op, a conflicting terminal fails, a committed token has exactly one `MarkerRef`, and an aborted token can never later commit. In W12, every prepared participant names one committed `GlobalAttemptRegistration`, and its token/attempt has exactly one meta-Raft terminal `GlobalTxnRecord`; no shard can create or reverse that outcome | commit/meta+participant state-machine models + absent/submitted/abort race + cross-session retry/leader-loss/crash/partition idempotency oracle |
| FG-INV-02 | At most one legal owner holds an exclusive block/constraint lock at a time, and ownership is fenced against reuse | lock model + independent lock-table/fence oracle |
| FG-INV-03 | Every physical version chain is finite, acyclic, strictly newer-first by commit order, and points only within its owning object generation | Lean chain model + arena decode/debug/fuzz oracle |
| FG-INV-04 | Visibility obeys snapshot high sequence **and** each graph-reference role's selected branch ancestry, create/retire semantics, coordinate schema binding, and own-write rules; repeated references to one branch at distinct heads cannot alias | independent reference engine + Lean visibility model + historical-self-join/in-sim oracle |
| FG-INV-05 | Every committed SERIALIZABLE history has an acyclic logical dependency graph; SSI metadata remains until no overlapping transaction can add an edge. W12's meta-owned conflict index includes every local/cross-shard/read-only `wr`/`ww`/`rw` edge and may commit a candidate only after independent recomputation proves adding it remains acyclic | independent local+global SCC/history oracle + overlap-lifetime oracle + scoped Lean theorem |
| FG-INV-06 | Every witness conservatively covers its logical positive, negative, gap, early-stop, and path-cut observations; refinement preserves them. Partition routing/coarsening preserves the same `concretization`/`may_affect` contract across all W12 participants, and missing routing or support is conservative failure, never a dropped edge | constructor/refinement/partition-transport proofs + mutation-complete single/multi-shard small-model differential suite |
| FG-INV-07 | The durable strong/uncut-conditional object graph is acyclic and each edge or weak digest names already identified bytes. Genesis reaches `Operational` only through the ordered checkpoint/floor bootstrap. Before any receipt/order, D1 roots an exact base logical+encoding+placement closure under one stable `PreparedOwnershipId`; successors preserve or strengthen it. Every ordered transaction command strongly names final post-rebase effects/template, authorization, resource/outcome preparation, and an exact-configuration availability certificate; the role-valid Raft log retains it until deterministic apply constructs result objects → payload → matching command record/marker → root. In W12, registration precedes reads; effect-only bases → routing certificate → aggregate authorization/resource/outcome/audit → fragments → shard prepare commands/records/certificates → serialization/constraint certificates → meta pre-command-base certificate → global command is the only legal decision input order. Meta apply constructs marker/outcome/payload → global transaction record → global root; afterward it constructs and meta-publishes the decision certificate; shard apply constructs fragment batches/acks; only then does a global-delta object → publish command → payload/control record/root advance Ripple. Every cross-group edge is certified remote and every prepared/certificate closure remains owned through terminal apply/GC. Control commands name only pre-order specs with weak CAS identities, never their results or retained prior roots. Prebuilt audit events commit only sequence-neutral transaction-effect or gate-excluding control-spec bodies and pre-order transition bases; they never digest the later gate/container/result that owns them. Receipt timeout never releases ownership | generated DAG/reference/digest-domain/bootstrap/registered-kind checker + role-tagged prepared-root/D1/D2/local+meta+shard Raft/checkpoint-install TLA+ model + audit-commitment-extension oracle + crash/reconfiguration/leader-loss/remote-retention matrix + command/availability verifier |
| FG-INV-08 | The complete logical-command predecessor order and transaction-marker subsequence are contiguous at their respective sequences; a retained checkpoint suffix starts with its exact install command; every role-tagged Raft snapshot root/configuration/sequences equal the state at its exact log cut; every branch-head CAS/parent link is valid. Local transparency claims only cached-client rollback detection; witnessed detection claims evidence after gossip/cross-log convergence; non-equivocation is claimed only for a fresh strongly named policy with `2t > n+f`, threshold-valid distinct configured keys, durable one-head witnesses, verified consistency extensions, and old+new thresholds at rotation. In W12 all semantic sequences/HLC and branch heads are issued only by meta-Raft, every shard applies or proves irrelevance through one contiguous global prefix while retaining the selected historical cut, and no shard-local order is semantic time | two-sequence checkpoint-install/local+meta+shard exact-cut/branch/barrier oracle + command/marker chain and MMR verifiers + isolated-quorum/equivocation/state-loss/stale-checkpoint/joint-rotation split-view tests |
| FG-INV-09 | Full `ObjectId` matches canonical plaintext; `CiphertextId` matches its complete descriptor/protected bytes; `EncodingId` matches the complete immutable decode/auth descriptor; `PlacementId` matches only its non-self-referential descriptor and exact inventory; root bootstrap reproduces that descriptor/inventory without indexes; metadata-child DEKs unwrap only under the exact reconstructible noncircular AAD transcript; each `SymbolRecord` MAC matches its full canonical transcript; locator collisions are resolved and distinct encodings never combine | decode/full-digest/descriptor/AAD oracle + root-bootstrap span/inventory closure checks + placement/metadata self-cycle schema check + collision/mixed-symbol/FEC-wire fuzz campaigns |
| FG-INV-10 | Under an accepted versioned filesystem profile and its declared crash model, publication leaves a highest structurally credible slot with an authentic mandatory local/logical/prepared closure, matching writer fence and any audit visibility fence/candidate, and complete durable/applied/visible positions. Before an ordinary `FenceToken` exists, only linear `PendingFenceGuard` may seal/publish the one state-preserving `epoch+1` fence root/slot and only `PendingCreationGuard` may seal the complete Genesis staging root and perform its `RENAME_NOREPLACE`+directory-sync installation; neither can express any user segment, receipt, Raft, canonical transition, or general root. Reread consumes the pending guard into the live token, after which every ordinary seal, prepared-root update, receipt, Raft proposal/ack, or root publication requires that token and lease; older receipted/ordered obligations remain rooted. Bootstrap phase/optional roots have only the three legal states. Every local/meta/shard checkpoint vector classifies every payload field and hashes a non-self-referential basis projection; operational vectors replace checkpoint/floor through literals without retaining a prior install chain. Authenticated closure failure never causes implicit rollback and instead repairs or fails closed | filesystem-profile/lease/takeover/pending-guard type model + existing-takeover and staging-create `O_EXCL`/`RENAME_NOREPLACE` crash matrices + root/bootstrap/all-role paired-checkpoint-floor/schema-coverage/prepared/audit-fence models + every-write/directory/fsync-lie/path-replacement/fencing/rollback/reset/retention-chain tests |
| FG-INV-11 | Externally monotonic allocation epochs plus canonical allocator/range state prevent VId/EId alias or reuse across crash, branch, clone, and same-identity rollback restore; labels never change identity; canonical forward incidence, stable IDs/`OriginBirthOrder`s/branch-admission orders, membership, properties, ordinal maps, and branch-aware holes agree. Every declared/present reverse materialization agrees with forward truth, and its absence uses the exact fallback rather than changing results | external-continuity CAS/rollback model + allocator crash/restore/branch/merge oracle + reference graph each snapshot + forward/reverse-present/reverse-absent compaction/label/map metamorphics |
| FG-INV-12 | Canonical scalar equality/hash/order/encoding laws are coherent. Every transition claimed answer-equivalent—seal, compact, codec switch, spill, factorize/flatten, or safe replan—preserves logical value, multiplicity, order, visibility, and `AnswerContract`; an exact index rebuild preserves exact contents, while any approximate candidate/topology change creates a new pinned semantic generation rather than claiming physical equivalence | scalar-law property/fuzz suite + digest/reference equivalence + answer-contract/type checker + exact and approximate-generation metamorphic operators |
| FG-INV-13 | Commits are immutable; branch heads move only by atomic expected-head updates. Fork apply closes parent envelope/write epochs before opening independent parent/child successors, and every envelope edge/object-DEK/recipient wrap is bound to one authenticated root/cut/epoch, so a child or sibling cannot decrypt post-fork parent/other-branch data. A merge token/nonce/capability generation is pre-minted before deterministic apply and has one original terminal outcome, and target-basis-independent `ImportedRangeKey` coverage prevents exact or partial source-range reapplication across head drift, checkpoint cuts, restore, and reconfiguration. Merge effects obey proved ACI algebra or the recorded total order | branch/fork-key-envelope/merge/token-generation/imported-coverage model + cross-branch decryption-denial/AAD/entropy-boundary/head-drift/overlap/subtract-policy/history-cut/backup/retry property tests |
| FG-INV-14 | GC follows every typed strong/uncut conditional reference and treats locator/placement/remote-observation/checkpoint-floor-observation and covered-checkpoint-command identities as nonretaining. A live `StrongCiphertextRef` retains its exact ciphertext, opener, selected recoverable encoding/placement set, and certificate; re-encryption is not a substitute. A `CertifiedRemoteStrongRef` is nonlocal ownership, not a weak observation: referrer and authority floors release it only by two-sided acknowledged transfer/GC. No object/key/effect reachable from credible roots, schema-complete checkpoints/floors, prepared/certificate ledgers/Raft, branches/bases/key-epoch/envelope/grant/merge roots, cursors/leases, backup/legal hold, replay, audit/transparency, transaction/resource/DP/continuity state, or W12 registration/decision/conflict/reservation/prepare/checkpoint/delta/topology obligations is reclaimed or cryptographically destroyed. Installed floors use weak current-checkpoint evidence, operational projections exclude prior floors, cut identities never retain old roots accidentally, and two-stage key finalization proves zero references over this universe | consensus+two-sided-remote GC/generated-reference-kind/ciphertext-realization/key-destruction model + mark-then-resolution oracle + paired-checkpoint/no-retention-chain + reconfiguration/prepared/sharded-decision/cursor-delivery/replay/continuity/grant-reencryption/key-rotation storms |
| FG-INV-15 | For every registered exact derivative, integrating ordered deltas equals batch evaluation. A retained local `LogicalDeltaBatch` weakly identifies source template/marker but strongly owns every base payload, integrates every relevant coordinate exactly once, and publishes one frontier/root or none. In W12 the decision record never names a future batch: after every exact participant batch/ack exists, one acyclic `GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch` owns the complete certified-remote set for one global marker, and only its meta-ordered publish control may advance Ripple; no shard/frontier publishes it partially. A baseline public digest covers its exact authorized coverage/frontier/schema/contract/result bytes; every atomic/coalesced delta envelope separately commits complete source provenance and strongly owns a typed delivered-output payload whose public digest covers exact authorized schema/contract/Z-set bytes; keyed object IDs are never treated as client-verifiable. A durable cursor generation plus one tagged baseline-or-delta lease makes create/baseline-ACK/rotate/delta-ACK/lost-response/resume/reset/expiry idempotent, retains exact promised bytes until terminal, and emits no delta before baseline ACK; gaps are explicit. Derived reads obey coverage and compositional result contracts, and hidden/future ANN nodes cannot influence authorized results | derivative-vs-local+post-decision-global-publish differential + DAG/participant-completeness/two-sided-reachability/frontier oracle + baseline/delivered-output/envelope/public-digest/chunk/cursor-generation/lease/coalesce/ACK-resume tests + answer-contract/index/ANN suites |
| FG-INV-16 | Safety: no task, pin, scratch object, resume cursor/baseline-or-delta lease/payload/envelope, prepared/receipted command closure, externally charged privacy debit/request tombstone/seed/result, externally reserved audit ticket/event/resolution/CAS receipt/gap transition, or resource charge is lost, duplicated, refunded, released, or exposed while obligated. Audit admission verifies the exact external `TicketIssued` successor; every protected transaction/control event and terminal gate is prebuilt and byte-matched; an audit-fenced candidate root/result remains invisible until a mirror verifies the exact direct external successor for the same ticket/request/event/outcome/candidate; lifecycle commands cannot recurse. Same-identity restore reconciles external privacy and audit continuity before gated operations; missing evidence requires a durable permanent-gap transition that forever bounds future claims. Liveness: each reaches a legal terminal/recovered state under registered fairness, eventual-storage/network/continuity-authority recovery, quorum, and resource assumptions | asupersync leak oracle + prepared/resource/baseline-cursor-delivery/DP/audit-admission/control-event/chain-visibility/scratch/commit recovery tests + external-CAS stale-head/substitution/rollback/gap reconciliation and bounded-liveness models |
| FG-INV-17 | Rebase and branch merge are capability-stripped and deterministic under the pinned `IntentSemanticsOid`; every semantic change regenerates final effects, reads/writes, constraints, witnesses, logical deltas, and a new capsule before publication | type boundaries + unavailable/wrong-semantics fail-closed tests + effect-digest oracle + forced-drift replay/property tests |
| FG-INV-18 | Base semantics and constraints remain authoritative: canonical `CommittedEffectSet` equals the logical before/after change; constraint writes cannot commit without synchronous enforcement; rebuildable indexes/views may be discarded | reference-effect differential + degraded-recovery/constraint rebuild drills |
| FG-INV-19 | A registry-rooted manifest's structural maximum is derived only by its versioned evidence-slot matrix, and its live effective grade may only weaken under resolution/lease/trust/authority state. Effective `Replayable` requires every semantic slot to be a live typed local/archive object—including answer requirement, realized contract, authority, external inputs, executable artifacts, decisions, and exact approximate generations—and reproduces the canonical logical result. Structural replay requires its typed projection; supply-later omissions carry expected identities/digests; audit/redacted/expired closures carry only their derived weaker grade. Answer-affecting and canonical-state-affecting policies are sequenced/pinned; proved answer-equivalent physical layout/framing cannot change strict output | cross-plan/target/artifact/approximate-generation replay CI + generated slot-grade/live-resolution/archive-expiry/registry-root closure doctor + replica logical-digest oracle |
| FG-INV-20 | Authorization is end-to-end before observation or effect across storage, statistics, routing/scoring, mutation/errors, local or cross-shard constraints/witnesses/prepares, derived state, Prism/UDFs, streams and all four cross-session capability kinds, replay evidence/resolvers, export/backup, externally continuous audit, and observability. Authorization's ticket-only gate precedes the event; every ticket-gated local/global transaction/control mutation carries the exact terminal triple and typed outcome. W12 computes the effect-only participant basis first, then exactly one current union-wide `GlobalAuthorizationDecisionRecord` and one matching global ticket/event/resolution over all routed effects, hidden cascades, heads/key epochs, constraints and resources; every fragment/prepare binds those same records, and no set of merely local approvals can substitute. Lifecycle exceptions are fixed non-user structural cases. Hidden-state constraint behavior obeys one explicit `ConstraintDisclosureContract`; only its named, ticketed and audited declassification is permitted | unforgeable secure-view/gate/capability/aggregate-record types + single/multi-shard omitted-participant/cross-capability/noninterference/declassification/audit-admission/terminal/continuity matrix + Warden fuzz/model tests |

### Statistical, evidence, and configuration gates (not invariants)

| ID | Qualified claim | Required disclosure/gate |
|---|---|---|
| FG-CAL-01 | Adaptive policy evidence versus pinned fallback | null/outcome filtration, alpha, support/overlap, effective sample size, loss and fallback; stream-sequenced promotion only |
| FG-CAL-02 | Cardinality/risk interval coverage | population, selection/window, exchangeability or nonexchangeability method, strata, marginal target, realized coverage and drift |
| FG-CAL-03 | ANN recall/drift evidence | authorized snapshot population, keyed sample, exact baseline, candidate policy, confidence interval and rebuild action |
| FG-EVID-01 | Decision-card/OPE completeness | state/actions/features, logged probabilities, zero-support exclusions, clipping/estimator, policy epoch and fallback |
| FG-EVID-02 | Scrub/corpus-health evidence | population, keyed stratified sampling, dependence assumptions, exhaustive-sweep position and observed corruption |
| FG-CFG-01 | Modeled durability target | CTMC/model version, fitted failure rates, failure domains, sensitivity bounds, repair/backup assumptions |
| FG-CFG-02 | Modeled controller stability | model/equilibrium, parameter uncertainty, predicted margin, deterministic hard guards and soak results |
| FG-CFG-03 | View/index staleness SLO feasibility | arrival/service assumptions, resource reservation, predicted envelope, actual watermark and fallback policy |

*Fin. The graph database the 2030s deserve, built from parts the 2020s already proved — ours.*
